Expand: (p - u/2)^2 + 2v t_C (p - u/2) + v^2 t_C^2 + (v/2 + u t_C)^2 = (p - u/2)^2 + 2v t_D (p - u/2) + v^2 t_D^2 + (v/2 + u t_D)^2.

Cancel (p-u/2)^2. Then:

2v t_C (p - u/2) + v^2 t_C^2 + (v/2 + u t_C)^2 = 2v t_D (p - u/2) + v^2 t_D^2 + (v/2 + u t_D)^2.

Compute (v/2 + u t)^2 = v^2/4 + u v t + u^2 t^2.

So left: 2v t_C (p - u/2) + v^2 t_C^2 + v^2/4 + u v t_C + u^2 t_C^2 = 2v t_C (p - u/2) + v^2/4 + u v t_C + (v^2+u^2) t_C^2 = 2v t_C (p - u/2) + v^2/4 + u v t_C + d^2 t_C^2.

Similarly, right: 2v t_D (p - u/2) + v^2/4 + u v t_D + d^2 t_D^2.

2v t_C (p - u/2) + u v t_C + d^2 t_C^2 = 2v t_D (p - u/2) + u v t_D + d^2 t_D^2.

Bring terms with (p-u/2) together:

2v (p - u/2)(t_C - t_D) + u v (t_C - t_D) + d^2 (t_C^2 - t_D^2) = 0.

Since C and D are distinct (order implies t_C < t_D), t_C ≠ t_D. So we have:

2v(p - u/2) + u v + d^2 (t_C + t_D) = 0.

Thus:

2v(p - u/2) = -u v - d^2 (t_C + t_D).

Divide by v (v≠0 because A and B distinct and AB not horizontal? Actually if v=0 then B is on x-axis, but then AB is horizontal, and MN is vertical (perpendicular bisector). But in our coordinate choice, we have AP as x-axis; we cannot arbitrarily set AP as x-axis and also have P on x-axis; that is the definition. So we need to check if P lies on x-axis for the given configuration. In the candidate solution, they assumed that AP is the x-axis, so P is on x-axis. That's fine; we are free to choose coordinate system such that AP is x-axis. So we don't need to prove that P has y=0; we set it that way. So in our coordinate system, we already have P = (p,0). So the equation we derived from PC=PD is one condition that must be satisfied. We also have PA^2 = PC^2, which will give another equation that determines p.

So we have:

(1) PA^2 = PC^2: p^2 = (p - u/2 + v t_C)^2 + (v/2 + u t_C)^2.
(2) PC = PD gives the equation: 2v(p - u/2) + u v + d^2 (t_C + t_D) = 0.

We can use these to solve for p in terms of u,v,t_M,t_N. Then we also need to compute H and the tangency condition.

Let's compute (1) expanded:

p^2 = (p - u/2)^2 + 2v t_C (p - u/2) + v^2 t_C^2 + (v/2 + u t_C)^2 = (p - u/2)^2 + 2v t_C (p - u/2) + v^2 t_C^2 + v^2/4 + u v t_C + u^2 t_C^2 = (p - u/2)^2 + 2v t_C (p - u/2) + u v t_C + d^2 t_C^2 + v^2/4.

So p^2 = (p - u/2)^2 + u v t_C + 2v t_C (p - u/2) + d^2 t_C^2 + v^2/4.

But (p - u/2)^2 = p^2 - u p + u^2/4. So:

p^2 = p^2 - u p + u^2/4 + u v t_C + 2v t_C (p - u/2) + d^2 t_C^2 + v^2/4.

Cancel p^2. Then:

0 = -u p + u^2/4 + u v t_C + 2v t_C (p - u/2) + d^2 t_C^2 + v^2/4.

Compute 2v t_C (p - u/2) = 2v t_C p - u v t_C.

So:

0 = -u p + u^2/4 + u v t_C + 2v t_C p - u v t_C + d^2 t_C^2 + v^2/4.

The u v t_C terms cancel: u v t_C - u v t_C = 0. So we have:

0 = -u p + u^2/4 + 2v t_C p + d^2 t_C^2 + v^2/4.

Thus:

u p - 2v t_C p = u^2/4 + d^2 t_C^2 + v^2/4.

So:

p(u - 2v t_C) = u^2/4 + v^2/4 + d^2 t_C^2 = (u^2+v^2)/4 + d^2 t_C^2 = d^2/4 + d^2 t_C^2 = d^2 (t_C^2 + 1/4).

But note that d^2 (t_C^2+1/4) = r^2? Actually r = d √(t_M^2+1/4), and t_C = t_M - √(t_M^2+1/4). So t_C^2+1/4 is not obviously r^2/d^2. But we can also note that r^2 = d^2 (t_M^2+1/4). So t_C^2+1/4 =? We'll keep.

Thus:

p(u - 2v t_C) = d^2 (t_C^2 + 1/4).   (Equation A)

Now, from PC=PD we have:

2v(p - u/2) + u v + d^2 (t_C + t_D) = 0 => 2v p - u v + u v + d^2 (t_C + t_D) = 0 => 2v p + d^2 (t_C + t_D) = 0 => 2v p = -d^2 (t_C + t_D) => p = -d^2 (t_C + t_D) / (2v).   (Equation B)

Substitute this into Equation A:

(-d^2 (t_C + t_D) / (2v)) * (u - 2v t_C) = d^2 (t_C^2 + 1/4).

Cancel d^2 (nonzero). Then:

-(t_C + t_D)(u - 2v t_C) / (2v) = t_C^2 + 1/4.

Multiply both sides by 2v:

-(t_C + t_D)(u - 2v t_C) = 2v (t_C^2 + 1/4).

Thus:

(t_C + t_D)(u - 2v t_C) = -2v (t_C^2 + 1/4).   (Equation C)

Now, we also have t_C and t_D expressed in terms of t_M, t_N. t_C = t_M - √(t_M^2+1/4). t_D = t_N + √(t_N^2+1/4). So we can plug in.

But maybe we can find a simpler relation: Since P is circumcenter of ACD, and A is at origin, we might also have that P lies on the perpendicular bisector of CD, which is perpendicular to MN. But we already used PC=PD. So that gives p in terms of t_C,t_D. So we have an expression for p.

Now, we need to find H, orthocenter of triangle PMN. Coordinates: P=(p,0), M=(u/2 - v t_M, v/2 + u t_M), N=(u/2 - v t_N, v/2 + u t_N). The orthocenter H is the intersection of altitudes. Since P has y=0, we can find H. There is a known formula: For triangle with vertices (x1,y1), (x2,y2), (x3,y3), the orthocenter is (x1+x2+x3 - 2*(circumcenter_x)? Not sure. Alternatively, we can compute using altitudes: Altitude from P is perpendicular to MN, so its equation is line through P with direction perpendicular to MN. Since MN direction is (-v, u), a perpendicular direction is (u, v). So altitude from P: (x,y) = (p,0) + λ(u, v). That is one line.

Altitude from M: perpendicular to PN. PN vector = N - P = (u/2 - v t_N - p, v/2 + u t_N - 0) = (u/2 - v t_N - p, v/2 + u t_N). So altitude from M is line through M with direction perpendicular to PN. But that is true if we consider vectors from circumcenter? Actually if O is circumcenter, then the vector from O to H is the sum of vectors from O to vertices: OH = OP + OM + ON. So H = O + (P-O) + (M-O) + (N-O) = P+M+N - 2O. So that is correct. So if we find circumcenter O of triangle PMN, we can compute H.

Also, the perpendicular bisector of PM is perpendicular to PM and passes through midpoint of PM. Intersection gives O. Then H = P+M+N-2O.

But we might compute H directly using altitude intersection. Let's attempt to compute H coordinates in terms of u,v, t_M, t_N, and p.

Define:

Let’s denote coordinates:

P = (p, 0)
M = (m_x, m_y) = (u/2 - v t_M, v/2 + u t_M)
N = (n_x, n_y) = (u/2 - v t_N, v/2 + u t_N)

The altitude from P: line through P perpendicular to MN. MN direction = (-v, u). So a direction vector for altitude is (u, v). So param: (x,y) = (p,0) + λ(u, v). So H lies on this line: H = (p + λ u, λ v) for some λ.

Now, we also need that H lies on altitude from M, which is perpendicular to PN. So vector PN = N - P = (n_x - p, n_y - 0) = (u/2 - v t_N - p, v/2 + u t_N). So direction of altitude from M is perpendicular to PN: it is vector ( -n_y, n_x - p ) (since perpendicular to (dx,dy) is (-dy,dx)). So line through M with direction ( -n_y, n_x - p ): (x,y) = (m_x, m_y) + μ ( -n_y, n_x - p ). H must satisfy both.

So we can set:

p + λ u = m_x + μ (-n_y)
λ v = m_y + μ (n_x - p)

We can solve for λ and μ. We have unknowns λ, μ. Solve the system:

From first: μ = (p + λ u - m_x) / (-n_y) = (m_x - p - λ u) / n_y. (Provided n_y ≠ 0; we can handle n_y=0 separately.)

Plug into second: λ v = m_y + ((m_x - p - λ u) / n_y) * (n_x - p).

Multiply both sides by n_y:

λ v n_y = m_y n_y + (m_x - p - λ u)(n_x - p).

Thus:

λ v n_y = m_y n_y + (m_x - p)(n_x - p) - λ u (n_x - p).

Bring λ terms together:

λ v n_y + λ u (n_x - p) = m_y n_y + (m_x - p)(n_x - p).

So:

λ [ v n_y + u (n_x - p) ] = m_y n_y + (m_x - p)(n_x - p).

Thus:

λ = [ m_y n_y + (m_x - p)(n_x - p) ] / [ v n_y + u (n_x - p) ].

Then H = (p + λ u, λ v).

Now, we need to show that the horizontal line y = λ v is tangent to circumcircle of BEF. So we need to compute the circumcircle of BEF, find its center and radius, and show that the distance from that center to the horizontal line equals the radius.

Points: B = (u, v), E = (u - 2v t_M, 0), F = (u - 2v t_N, 0). So E and F are on x-axis, B is above (or below) x-axis. The circumcircle of BEF: we can find its equation. Since E and F are on x-axis, the perpendicular bisector of EF is vertical line x = (x_E + x_F)/2 = ( (u-2v t_M)+(u-2v t_N) )/2 = u - v(t_M+t_N). So the center O_BEF lies on this vertical line: O = ( u - v(t_M+t_N), y0 ) for some y0. Also, it is equidistant from B and E. So we have:

Distance squared from O to E: (x_O - x_E)^2 + y0^2 = ( (u - v(t_M+t_N)) - (u - 2v t_M) )^2 + y0^2 = ( -v(t_M+t_N) + 2v t_M )^2 + y0^2 = ( v(t_M - t_N) )^2 + y0^2.

Distance squared from O to B: (x_O - u)^2 + (y0 - v)^2 = ( (u - v(t_M+t_N)) - u )^2 + (y0 - v)^2 = ( -v(t_M+t_N) )^2 + (y0 - v)^2 = v^2 (t_M+t_N)^2 + (y0 - v)^2.

Set these equal:

v^2 (t_M - t_N)^2 + y0^2 = v^2 (t_M+t_N)^2 + (y0 - v)^2.

Expand:

v^2 (t_M^2 - 2t_M t_N + t_N^2) + y0^2 = v^2 (t_M^2 + 2t_M t_N + t_N^2) + y0^2 - 2v y0 + v^2.

Cancel y0^2:

v^2 (t_M^2 - 2t_M t_N + t_N^2) = v^2 (t_M^2 + 2t_M t_N + t_N^2) - 2v y0 + v^2.

Thus:

v^2 (t_M^2 - 2t_M t_N + t_N^2) = v^2 (t_M^2 + 2t_M t_N + t_N^2) - 2v y0 + v^2.

Bring terms:

Left minus right: 0 = v^2 (t_M^2+2t_M t_N+t_N^2) - 2v y0 + v^2 - v^2 (t_M^2-2t_M t_N+t_N^2) = v^2 (4t_M t_N) - 2v y0 + v^2.

So:

4v^2 t_M t_N - 2v y0 + v^2 = 0.

Divide by v (v≠0): 4v t_M t_N - 2 y0 + v = 0 => 2 y0 = 4v t_M t_N + v => y0 = v (2 t_M t_N + 1/2) = v (2 t_M t_N + 1/2). So the center O_BEF = ( u - v(t_M+t_N), v(2 t_M t_N + 1/2) ).

Now, the radius R_BEF = distance from O to E: sqrt( v^2 (t_M - t_N)^2 + y0^2 ). So R_BEF = sqrt( v^2 (t_M - t_N)^2 + v^2 (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2 ) = |v| sqrt( (t_M - t_N)^2 + (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2 ). Since v is not zero (A and B distinct, and we can assume v>0 by orientation? Actually we can choose coordinates such that v>0. But the absolute value will be fine; we can take v>0.

Now, the line through H parallel to AP: AP is x-axis, so horizontal line y = y_H = λ v (since H = (p+λu, λv) from altitude param). So we need to show that this horizontal line is tangent to circle (BEF). That means the distance from the center O_BEF to the line y = λ v equals the radius. The center has y-coordinate y0 = v(2 t_M t_N + 1/2). So distance = |y0 - λ v| = |v(2 t_M t_N + 1/2) - λ v| = |v| |2 t_M t_N + 1/2 - λ|. Since v>0, we need |2 t_M t_N + 1/2 - λ| = R_BEF / v = sqrt( (t_M - t_N)^2 + (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2 ).

So we need to verify that λ satisfies: |2 t_M t_N + 1/2 - λ| = sqrt( (t_M - t_N)^2 + (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2 ). Since the RHS is positive, we need to show that (2 t_M t_N + 1/2 - λ)^2 = (t_M - t_N)^2 + (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2.

This simplifies to: (2 t_M t_N + 1/2 - λ)^2 = (t_M - t_N)^2 + (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2.

Expand left: (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2 - 2λ(2 t_M t_N + 1/2) + λ^2. Right: (t_M - t_N)^2 + (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2.

Cancel (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2 on both sides, we get:

-2λ(2 t_M t_N + 1/2) + λ^2 = (t_M - t_N)^2.

Thus:

λ^2 - 2λ(2 t_M t_N + 1/2) - (t_M - t_N)^2 = 0? Actually -2λ(2 t_M t_N+1/2) + λ^2 = (t_M - t_N)^2 => λ^2 - 2λ(2 t_M t_N+1/2) - (t_M - t_N)^2 = 0? Wait, we have λ^2 - 2λ(2 t_M t_N+1/2) = (t_M - t_N)^2. So that is the equation.

Thus we need to show that λ satisfies λ^2 - 2λ(2 t_M t_N+1/2) - (t_M - t_N)^2 = 0? Actually it's λ^2 - 2λ(2 t_M t_N+1/2) - (t_M - t_N)^2 = 0? Let's check: λ^2 - 2λ(2 t_M t_N+1/2) = (t_M - t_N)^2 => λ^2 - 2λ(2 t_M t_N+1/2) - (t_M - t_N)^2 = 0. Yes.

So we need to verify that λ is a root of that quadratic.

Now, we have λ from orthocenter condition. So we need to compute λ in terms of t_M, t_N, u, v, and p. And then substitute p from earlier relations and show that λ satisfies that equation.

We have λ = [ m_y n_y + (m_x - p)(n_x - p) ] / [ v n_y + u (n_x - p) ].

Let's derive λ more directly using vector approach: For triangle with vertices P, M, N, the orthocenter H satisfies H = P + M + N - 2*O, where O is circumcenter. So if we find O, we can get H. Alternatively, we can compute H directly using altitude intersection: H lies on altitude from P, which is line through P with direction (u, v). So H = (p + λ u, λ v). Also, H lies on altitude from M: (H - M) · (N - P) = 0. So ( (p+λ u - m_x, λ v - m_y) ) · ( (n_x - p, n_y) ) = 0.

So we have:

(p+λ u - m_x)(n_x - p) + (λ v - m_y) n_y = 0.

This is a linear equation in λ. Solve for λ:

(p+λ u - m_x)(n_x - p) + (λ v - m_y) n_y = 0

=> (p - m_x)(n_x - p) + λ u (n_x - p) + λ v n_y - m_y n_y = 0

=> λ [ u (n_x - p) + v n_y ] = m_y n_y - (p - m_x)(n_x - p)

=> λ = [ m_y n_y - (p - m_x)(n_x - p) ] / [ u (n_x - p) + v n_y ].

Note the sign: In our earlier derivation, we had λ = [ m_y n_y + (m_x - p)(n_x - p) ] / [ v n_y + u (n_x - p) ]. Since (m_x - p)(n_x - p) = -(p - m_x)(n_x - p). So that is m_y n_y - (p - m_x)(n_x - p). So it's the same. So good.

Thus λ = [ m_y n_y - (p - m_x)(n_x - p) ] / [ u (n_x - p) + v n_y ].

Now, we need to show that λ satisfies λ^2 - 2λ(2 t_M t_N+1/2) - (t_M - t_N)^2 = 0.

Let's compute everything in terms of t_M, t_N, u, v. Also p is expressed in terms of t_M, t_N, u, v via the circumcenter condition. Now, we have λ = [ m_y n_y - (p - m_x)(n_x - p) ] / [ u (n_x - p) + v n_y ].

Let's compute m_y n_y and (p - m_x)(n_x - p) and the denominator.

m_y = v/2 + u t_M
n_y = v/2 + u t_N

So m_y n_y = (v/2 + u t_M)(v/2 + u t_N) = v^2/4 + (u v/2)(t_M+t_N) + u^2 t_M t_N.

Now, compute (p - m_x)(n_x - p). m_x = u/2 - v t_M, n_x = u/2 - v t_N.

So p - m_x = p - u/2 + v t_M
n_x - p = u/2 - v t_N - p

Thus (p - m_x)(n_x - p) = (p - u/2 + v t_M)(u/2 - v t_N - p) = (p - u/2 + v t_M)( (u/2 - p) - v t_N ) = (p - u/2 + v t_M)( (u/2 - p) - v t_N ). Let’s denote A = p - u/2. Then (p - u/2 + v t_M) = A + v t_M, and (u/2 - p) = -A. So n_x - p = -A - v t_N. So product = (A + v t_M)(-A - v t_N) = -(A + v t_M)(A + v t_N). Actually careful: (A + v t_M)(-A - v t_N) = -(A + v t_M)(A + v t_N). So (p - m_x)(n_x - p) = - (A + v t_M)(A + v t_N).

Thus m_y n_y - (p - m_x)(n_x - p) = m_y n_y + (A + v t_M)(A + v t_N).

Now, m_y n_y = v^2/4 + (u v/2)(t_M+t_N) + u^2 t_M t_N.
(A + v t_M)(A + v t_N) = A^2 + A v (t_M+t_N) + v^2 t_M t_N.

So sum: m_y n_y - (p - m_x)(n_x - p) = v^2/4 + (u v/2)(t_M+t_N) + u^2 t_M t_N + A^2 + A v (t_M+t_N) + v^2 t_M t_N.

Thus numerator = A^2 + (u v/2 + A v)(t_M+t_N) + (u^2+v^2) t_M t_N + v^2/4 = A^2 + v( u/2 + A)(t_M+t_N) + d^2 t_M t_N + v^2/4.

Now, denominator: u (n_x - p) + v n_y = u ( -A - v t_N ) + v ( v/2 + u t_N ) = -u A - u v t_N + v^2/2 + u v t_N = -u A + v^2/2. Because -u v t_N + u v t_N cancel. So denominator = v^2/2 - u A.

Thus λ = [ A^2 + v( u/2 + A)(t_M+t_N) + d^2 t_M t_N + v^2/4 ] / [ v^2/2 - u A ].

Now, we need to find A = p - u/2. But p is expressed in terms of t_M,t_N, u,v. We can also find A from the circumcenter condition. We have earlier from PC=PD: 2v p + d^2(t_C+t_D)=0 => p = -d^2(t_C+t_D)/(2v). So A = p - u/2 = -d^2(t_C+t_D)/(2v) - u/2.

But also we have the relation from PA=PC: p(u - 2v t_C) = d^2 (t_C^2+1/4). That could give another expression for p. Possibly we can find A in terms of t_M,t_N directly.

Note that t_C = t_M - √(t_M^2+1/4). Let’s denote s_M = √(t_M^2+1/4). So t_C = t_M - s_M. Also t_D = t_N + s_N, where s_N = √(t_N^2+1/4). So t_C + t_D = t_M + t_N - s_M + s_N? Actually t_C+t_D = (t_M - s_M) + (t_N + s_N) = t_M + t_N + (s_N - s_M). So p = -d^2 (t_M + t_N + s_N - s_M) / (2v). Then A = p - u/2 = -d^2 (t_M + t_N + s_N - s_M)/(2v) - u/2.

Observations:

1. Since C and D are points on the line of centers MN, and A is on both circles, the circle through A, C, D is the circle with diameter? Not necessarily.

2. Points E and F are the second intersections of line AP with Ω and Γ. So by power of point A with respect to circles? Actually A is on both circles, so power is zero.

3. We can consider the homothety at A that sends Ω to Γ? Not exactly, because circles intersect, so they are not homothetic from A unless A is the center of similitude? The radical axis is AB. The centers M and N lie on the perpendicular bisector of AB.

4. Perhaps we can use the fact that the circumcircle of triangle BEF is orthogonal to something? Or that it is the circle with diameter the segment joining the orthocenters of triangles? Not sure.

Another idea: Use inversion about A. Let’s invert with respect to circle centered at A with arbitrary radius. Under inversion, circles through A become lines. So Ω and Γ become lines (since they pass through A). The line MN is the line through the centers; under inversion, it becomes a circle through A? Actually inversion maps lines not through A to circles through A. So MN (line not through A) becomes a circle through A. The points C and D are on MN and on circles through A, so under inversion, C and D become intersections of the images. The circumcircle of ACD becomes line through the images of C and D? Since circle through A inverts to line. So P, the circumcenter of ACD, is the center of that circle; under inversion, the center does not map to the center of the image line. So maybe not.

We could also consider the reflection across the perpendicular bisector of AB? That would swap M and N? Not sure.

Given the time, I think a coordinate proof is feasible and rigorous if we carry out the algebra. However, the candidate solution's algebraic verification was omitted. We can present a complete coordinate proof with careful algebra.

Let's set up coordinates:

Let A = (0,0). Let line AP be the x-axis, so P = (p,0) with p>0. Let B = (u,v) with v ≠ 0 (since A and B distinct, and we can orient such that v>0). The line MN is the perpendicular bisector of AB, so its equation is ux + vy = (u^2+v^2)/2. A direction vector for MN is (-v, u). So we can param: (x,y) = (u/2, v/2) + t*(-v, u). So points on MN are (u/2 - v t, v/2 + u t). Let M = (u/2 - v t_M, v/2 + u t_M) and N = (u/2 - v t_N, v/2 + u t_N) for some real t_M, t_N. Since the radius of Ω is less than that of Γ, we have r < R, and the order C,M,N,D implies t_M < t_N? Actually from earlier, we had t_C = t_M - r/d < t_M < t_N < t_D = t_N + R/d. So t_M < t_N. So t_M < t_N.

Now, we have circles: Ω: center M, radius r = distance from M to A. So r^2 = (u/2 - v t_M)^2 + (v/2 + u t_M)^2 = d^2(t_M^2+1/4), where d^2 = u^2+v^2. So r = d √(t_M^2+1/4). Similarly, R = d √(t_N^2+1/4).

Points C and D are the intersections of line MN with Ω and Γ respectively, with order C,M,N,D. So:

C = (u/2 - v t_C, v/2 + u t_C) with t_C = t_M - r/d = t_M - √(t_M^2+1/4).
D = (u/2 - v t_D, v/2 + u t_D) with t_D = t_N + R/d = t_N + √(t_N^2+1/4).

Now, P is the circumcenter of triangle ACD. Since A = (0,0), P = (p,0). The condition that P is equidistant from A, C, D gives:

PA^2 = p^2.
PC^2 = (p - (u/2 - v t_C))^2 + (0 - (v/2 + u t_C))^2.
PD^2 = (p - (u/2 - v t_D))^2 + (0 - (v/2 + u t_D))^2.

Set PC^2 = PD^2 and PC^2 = PA^2.

From PC^2 = PD^2, after simplification (as we did earlier), we obtain:

2v p + d^2(t_C + t_D) = 0.   (1)

From PC^2 = PA^2, we obtain:

p^2 = (p - u/2 + v t_C)^2 + (v/2 + u t_C)^2. Expanding and simplifying yields:

p(u - 2v t_C) = d^2(t_C^2 + 1/4).   (2)

Now, using the expressions for t_C and t_D in terms of t_M, t_N, we can express p in terms of t_M, t_N, u, v.

From (1): p = -d^2(t_C + t_D)/(2v). And t_C + t_D = t_M - √(t_M^2+1/4) + t_N + √(t_N^2+1/4) = t_M + t_N + (√(t_N^2+1/4) - √(t_M^2+1/4)). So p = -d^2(t_M+t_N + (√(t_N^2+1/4) - √(t_M^2+1/4)))/(2v).   (3)

Now, also from (2): p = d^2(t_C^2+1/4)/(u - 2v t_C). We could also substitute t_C^2+1/4 = 2t_M t_C + 1/2 from earlier? Actually we derived: t_C^2+1/4 = 2t_M t_C + 1/2. Let's verify: t_C = t_M - s_M, s_M = √(t_M^2+1/4). Then t_C^2+1/4 = (t_M - s_M)^2 + 1/4 = t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + s_M^2 + 1/4 = t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + (t_M^2+1/4) + 1/4 = 2t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + 1/2 = 2t_M(t_M - s_M) + 1/2 = 2t_M t_C + 1/2. So yes. So (2) becomes:

p(u - 2v t_C) = d^2(2 t_M t_C + 1/2).   (2')

Now, we also have from (1) that p = -d^2(t_C+t_D)/(2v). So we have two expressions for p. But maybe we can find a simpler expression for p in terms of t_M and t_N. Let's compute p from (1) and then see if we can find a relation between t_M and t_N from (2').

Alternatively, we can solve for p by eliminating t_C and t_D. Note that t_C and t_D are defined in terms of t_M and t_N. So p is directly given by (3). That is fine.

Now, we need to find H, the orthocenter of triangle PMN.

We have P = (p,0), M = (u/2 - v t_M, v/2 + u t_M), N = (u/2 - v t_N, v/2 + u t_N).

Let’s denote coordinates:

M = (m_x, m_y) = (u/2 - v t_M, v/2 + u t_M)
N = (n_x, n_y) = (u/2 - v t_N, v/2 + u t_N)

The altitude from P is perpendicular to MN. Since MN direction is (-v, u), a perpendicular direction is (u, v). So line through P with direction (u, v) is: (x,y) = (p,0) + λ(u, v). So H = (p+λ u, λ v) for some λ.

The altitude from M is perpendicular to PN. So (H - M) · (N - P) = 0.

Compute N - P = (n_x - p, n_y - 0) = (u/2 - v t_N - p, v/2 + u t_N). Let’s denote A = p - u/2 as before. Then n_x - p = -A - v t_N, and n_y = v/2 + u t_N.

Also, H - M = (p+λ u - m_x, λ v - m_y). m_x = u/2 - v t_M, so p+λ u - m_x = (p - u/2) + λ u + v t_M = A + λ u + v t_M. And m_y = v/2 + u t_M, so λ v - m_y = λ v - v/2 - u t_M = v(λ - 1/2) - u t_M.

Thus (H-M)·(N-P) = (A + λ u + v t_M)(-A - v t_N) + (v(λ - 1/2) - u t_M)(v/2 + u t_N) = 0.

Expand:

First term: (A + λ u + v t_M)(-A - v t_N) = -(A + λ u + v t_M)(A + v t_N) = -[ (A+λ u+v t_M)A + (A+λ u+v t_M)v t_N ] = -[ A^2 + A λ u + A v t_M + A v t_N + λ u v t_N + v^2 t_M t_N ] = -[ A^2 + A λ u + A v(t_M+t_N) + λ u v t_N + v^2 t_M t_N ].

Second term: (v(λ - 1/2) - u t_M)(v/2 + u t_N) = (v(λ - 1/2))(v/2+u t_N) - u t_M(v/2+u t_N) = v(λ - 1/2)*v/2 + v(λ - 1/2)*u t_N - u t_M v/2 - u^2 t_M t_N = v^2(λ - 1/2)/2 + u v t_N (λ - 1/2) - u v t_M/2 - u^2 t_M t_N.

So sum = 0:

- [ A^2 + A λ u + A v(t_M+t_N) + λ u v t_N + v^2 t_M t_N ] + [ v^2(λ - 1/2)/2 + u v t_N (λ - 1/2) - u v t_M/2 - u^2 t_M t_N ] = 0.

Multiply out the second term: v^2(λ - 1/2)/2 = v^2 λ/2 - v^2/4. So:

- A^2 - A λ u - A v(t_M+t_N) - λ u v t_N - v^2 t_M t_N + v^2 λ/2 - v^2/4 + u v t_N λ - u v t_N/2 - u v t_M/2 - u^2 t_M t_N = 0.

Now, combine terms with λ: - A λ u - λ u v t_N + v^2 λ/2 + u v t_N λ = λ[ -A u - u v t_N + v^2/2 + u v t_N ] = λ[ -A u + v^2/2 ]. Because -u v t_N + u v t_N cancel. So λ term is λ(v^2/2 - A u).

Now, constant terms: - A^2 - A v(t_M+t_N) - v^2 t_M t_N - v^2/4 - u v t_N/2 - u v t_M/2 - u^2 t_M t_N.

So we have:

λ(v^2/2 - A u) + [ -A^2 - A v(t_M+t_N) - v^2 t_M t_N - v^2/4 - u v t_N/2 - u v t_M/2 - u^2 t_M t_N ] = 0.

Thus:

λ(v^2/2 - A u) = A^2 + A v(t_M+t_N) + v^2 t_M t_N + v^2/4 + u v t_N/2 + u v t_M/2 + u^2 t_M t_N.

Now, note that d^2 = u^2+v^2. So v^2 t_M t_N + u^2 t_M t_N = d^2 t_M t_N. So the RHS becomes:

A^2 + A v(t_M+t_N) + d^2 t_M t_N + v^2/4 + (u v/2)(t_M+t_N).

Thus:

λ(v^2/2 - A u) = A^2 + v( A + u/2 )(t_M+t_N) + d^2 t_M t_N + v^2/4.

This is the same as we had before, with denominator = v^2/2 - A u.

Thus λ = [ A^2 + v( A + u/2 )(t_M+t_N) + d^2 t_M t_N + v^2/4 ] / [ v^2/2 - A u ].   (4)

Now, we need to show that λ satisfies:

λ^2 - 2λ(2 t_M t_N + 1/2) - (t_M - t_N)^2 = 0.   (5)

We have A expressed in terms of t_M,t_N,u,v via (3). But maybe we can find a direct relation between A and the other variables from the circumcenter conditions. We have (2'): p(u - 2v t_C) = d^2(2 t_M t_C + 1/2). And p = A + u/2. So:

(A + u/2)(u - 2v t_C) = d^2(2 t_M t_C + 1/2).   (6)

We can also express t_C in terms of t_M: t_C = t_M - s_M, with s_M = √(t_M^2+1/4). So u - 2v t_C = u - 2v(t_M - s_M) = u - 2v t_M + 2v s_M. And 2 t_M t_C + 1/2 = 2 t_M(t_M - s_M) + 1/2 = 2 t_M^2 - 2 t_M s_M + 1/2 = 2 t_M^2 - 2 t_M s_M + 1/2. But note that s_M^2 = t_M^2+1/4, so 2 t_M^2 = 2 s_M^2 - 1/2. So 2 t_M t_C + 1/2 = (2 s_M^2 - 1/2) - 2 t_M s_M + 1/2 = 2 s_M^2 - 2 t_M s_M = 2 s_M (s_M - t_M) = 2 s_M t_C. So (2') becomes:

p(u - 2v t_C) = d^2 * 2 s_M t_C? Actually careful: d^2(2 t_M t_C + 1/2) = d^2 * 2 s_M t_C? Because 2 t_M t_C + 1/2 = 2 s_M t_C? Let's check: 2 s_M t_C = 2 s_M (t_M - s_M) = 2 s_M t_M - 2 s_M^2 = 2 s_M t_M - 2(t_M^2+1/4) = 2 s_M t_M - 2 t_M^2 - 1/2 = 2 t_M(s_M - t_M) - 1/2? Actually we need to verify equality: 2 t_M t_C + 1/2 = 2 t_M(t_M - s_M) + 1/2 = 2 t_M^2 - 2 t_M s_M + 1/2. And 2 s_M t_C = 2 s_M (t_M - s_M) = 2 t_M s_M - 2 s_M^2 = 2 t_M s_M - 2(t_M^2+1/4) = 2 t_M s_M - 2 t_M^2 - 1/2. So these are negatives: (2 t_M t_C + 1/2) = - (2 s_M t_C). So we have p(u - 2v t_C) = d^2 * (-2 s_M t_C). So p(u - 2v t_C) = -2 d^2 s_M t_C. But note that t_C is negative if t_M is positive? Actually t_C = t_M - s_M, which is negative because s_M > |t_M|? Not necessarily; if t_M is positive, s_M > t_M, so t_C < 0. If t_M is negative, t_C could be negative or positive? But s_M > |t_M|, so t_M - s_M is negative. So t_C < 0. So -2 d^2 s_M t_C is positive? Not important.

Anyway, we have a relation involving p and t_C. But we might also have a relation from (1): p = -d^2(t_C+t_D)/(2v). So we can substitute p.

Given the algebra, maybe we can find a direct expression for λ in terms of t_M,t_N. Let's try to compute λ using the condition that H is orthocenter, which gives an alternative expression: In triangle PMN, the orthocenter H can also be expressed as H = P + M + N - 2O, where O is circumcenter. Given the time, maybe we can attempt to verify the tangency condition using the expression for λ and the known relations, but we need to do it in a manageable way. Let's attempt to express everything in terms of t_M and t_N, and then simplify λ.

Let’s define:

This is an algebraic identity that we can try to verify by substituting the expression for A and simplifying. However, the presence of square roots s_M and s_N complicates things. Maybe there is a trick: Since the result is invariant under scaling and rotation, we can set specific coordinates to simplify the algebra. So we can set M = (m, b/2), N = (n, b/2). Since the radius of Ω is less than that of Γ, and the order C,M,N,D lies on MN, with C and D on the line MN (horizontal). Compute N - P = (n - p, b/2 - 0) = (n-p, b/2).
H - M = (p - m, y_H - b/2).
Dot: (p-m)(n-p) + (y_H - b/2)(b/2) = 0 => (p-m)(n-p) + (b/2)(y_H - b/2) = 0 => (b/2)(y_H - b/2) = -(p-m)(n-p) => y_H - b/2 = -2(p-m)(n-p)/b => y_H = b/2 - 2(p-m)(n-p)/b.

Thus H = (p, b/2 - 2(p-m)(n-p)/b).

Now, the line through H parallel to AP: AP is x-axis, so horizontal line y = y_H. So we need to show that this horizontal line is tangent to circumcircle of triangle BEF.

Points: B = (0,b). E = (2m,0). F = (2n,0). So triangle BEF: B(0,b), E(2m,0), F(2n,0). Its circumcircle: since E and F are on x-axis, the perpendicular bisector of EF is vertical line x = (2m+2n)/2 = m+n. So center O_BEF = (m+n, y0) for some y0. Also, equidistant from B and E: distance squared from O to B: (m+n - 0)^2 + (y0 - b)^2 = (m+n)^2 + (y0-b)^2. Distance squared from O to E: (m+n - 2m)^2 + (y0 - 0)^2 = (n-m)^2 + y0^2. Set equal:

(m+n)^2 + (y0-b)^2 = (n-m)^2 + y0^2.

Expand: (m^2+2mn+n^2) + (y0^2 - 2b y0 + b^2) = (n^2 - 2mn + m^2) + y0^2.

Cancel m^2+n^2 and y0^2: 2mn - 2b y0 + b^2 = -2mn => 2mn + 2mn = 2b y0 - b^2 => 4mn = 2b y0 - b^2 => 2b y0 = 4mn + b^2 => y0 = (4mn + b^2)/(2b) = (2mn)/b + b/2.

Thus center O = (m+n, (2mn)/b + b/2). Radius R = distance from O to E: sqrt( (m+n - 2m)^2 + (y0)^2 ) = sqrt( (n-m)^2 + y0^2 ). So R^2 = (n-m)^2 + y0^2.

Now, the line through H parallel to AP is horizontal: y = y_H. So distance from center to this line is |y0 - y_H|. We need to show that |y0 - y_H| = R.

Compute y0 - y_H = (2mn)/b + b/2 - [b/2 - 2(p-m)(n-p)/b] = (2mn)/b + b/2 - b/2 + 2(p-m)(n-p)/b = (2mn)/b + 2(p-m)(n-p)/b = (2/b)[ mn + (p-m)(n-p) ].

Thus |y0 - y_H| = (2/b) | mn + (p-m)(n-p) |.

We need to show that this equals sqrt( (n-m)^2 + y0^2 ).

So we need to verify:

(2/b)^2 ( mn + (p-m)(n-p) )^2 = (n-m)^2 + y0^2.

Compute y0^2 = ( (2mn)/b + b/2 )^2 = (4m^2 n^2)/b^2 + 2mn + b^2/4? Actually (a+b)^2 = a^2+2ab+b^2, with a=2mn/b, b=b/2. So a^2 = 4m^2 n^2/b^2, 2ab = 2*(2mn/b)*(b/2) = 2mn, b^2 = b^2/4. So y0^2 = 4m^2 n^2/b^2 + 2mn + b^2/4.

Thus RHS = (n-m)^2 + 4m^2 n^2/b^2 + 2mn + b^2/4 = (n^2 - 2mn + m^2) + 4m^2 n^2/b^2 + 2mn + b^2/4 = n^2 + m^2 + 4m^2 n^2/b^2 + b^2/4.

Because -2mn+2mn cancel. So RHS = m^2+n^2 + 4m^2 n^2/b^2 + b^2/4.

Now, LHS = (4/b^2)( mn + (p-m)(n-p) )^2. So we need to show that:

(4/b^2)( mn + (p-m)(n-p) )^2 = m^2+n^2 + 4m^2 n^2/b^2 + b^2/4.

Multiply both sides by b^2: 4( mn + (p-m)(n-p) )^2 = b^2(m^2+n^2) + 4m^2 n^2 + b^4/4.

Thus we need to verify that 4( mn + (p-m)(n-p) )^2 = b^2(m^2+n^2) + 4m^2 n^2 + b^4/4.

Now, we also have relations from the circumcenter condition: p = (m+n+R-r)/2 and p^2 = (p - m + r)^2 + b^2/4. Also, r^2 = m^2 + b^2/4, R^2 = n^2 + b^2/4. So we can try to express p in terms of m,n,b. Let's do that.

We have p = (m+n+R-r)/2 => 2p = m+n+R-r => R-r = 2p - m - n. (Equation A)

Also, from PA=PC: p^2 = (p - m + r)^2 + b^2/4. Expand: p^2 = (p - m)^2 + 2r(p-m) + r^2 + b^2/4. But (p-m)^2 = p^2 - 2pm + m^2. So p^2 = p^2 - 2pm + m^2 + 2r(p-m) + r^2 + b^2/4. Cancel p^2: 0 = -2pm + m^2 + 2r(p-m) + r^2 + b^2/4. So:

2r(p-m) = 2pm - m^2 - r^2 - b^2/4. (Equation B)

But note that r^2 = m^2 + b^2/4, so r^2 + b^2/4 = m^2 + b^2/2. Then 2pm - m^2 - (m^2 + b^2/2) = 2pm - 2m^2 - b^2/2. So (B) becomes:

2r(p-m) = 2pm - 2m^2 - b^2/2.

Thus r(p-m) = pm - m^2 - b^2/4. (Equation C)

Now, also we have R-r = 2p - m - n from (A). So R = r + 2p - m - n. Then square: R^2 = (r + 2p - m - n)^2. But also R^2 = n^2 + b^2/4. And r^2 = m^2 + b^2/4. So we can expand:

r^2 + 2r(2p - m - n) + (2p - m - n)^2 = n^2 + b^2/4.

Substitute r^2 = m^2 + b^2/4:

m^2 + b^2/4 + 2r(2p - m - n) + (2p - m - n)^2 = n^2 + b^2/4.

Cancel b^2/4: m^2 + 2r(2p - m - n) + (2p - m - n)^2 = n^2.

Thus:

2r(2p - m - n) = n^2 - m^2 - (2p - m - n)^2. (Equation D)

Now, we also have from (C): r(p-m) = pm - m^2 - b^2/4. We can try to eliminate r.

From (C): r = (pm - m^2 - b^2/4)/(p-m), provided p≠m. But note that p is circumcenter of ACD; likely p is not equal to m. Let's proceed.

Plug r into (D):

2 * ((pm - m^2 - b^2/4)/(p-m)) * (2p - m - n) = n^2 - m^2 - (2p - m - n)^2.

Multiply both sides by (p-m):

2(pm - m^2 - b^2/4)(2p - m - n) = (p-m)[ n^2 - m^2 - (2p - m - n)^2 ].

Now, note that n^2 - m^2 = (n-m)(n+m). Also, (2p - m - n)^2 = (2p - (m+n))^2. So RHS = (p-m)[ (n-m)(n+m) - (2p - m - n)^2 ].

We can also express (2p - m - n) in terms of p,m,n. This is getting messy but maybe we can find a simple expression for p.

So O satisfies:

O·(M-P) = (M^2 - P^2)/2
O·(N-P) = (N^2 - P^2)/2

These are two linear equations in the components of O. We can solve for O.

Let’s denote:

P = (p,0)
M = (m_x, m_y)
N = (n_x, n_y)

Then M-P = (m_x - p, m_y)
N-P = (n_x - p, n_y)

And we have:

O·(M-P) = (|M|^2 - p^2)/2
O·(N-P) = (|N|^2 - p^2)/2

We can solve for O using linear algebra. This is manageable if we have explicit expressions. Then H = P + M + N - 2O.

Let's proceed with this coordinate system: MN is x-axis, M=(m,0), N=(n,0) with m<n. A=(x_A, y_A) with y_A>0 (by orientation). Then B=(x_A, -y_A). C=(m - r, 0) with r^2 = (x_A - m)^2 + y_A^2. D=(n + R, 0) with R^2 = (x_A - n)^2 + y_A^2.

Now, P = circumcenter of ACD. Since C and D on x-axis, the perpendicular bisector of CD is vertical line x = (m - r + n + R)/2 = (m+n + (R-r))/2. So P has x-coordinate p = (m+n + (R-r))/2. Its y-coordinate is unknown; let P = (p, p_y). But also, P lies on perpendicular bisector of AC. So we can find p_y.

We also have that AP is the line through A and P. We can set the direction of AP; it's not necessarily horizontal.

Now, we need to compute H = orthocenter of triangle PMN. P=(p, p_y), M=(m,0), N=(n,0). So triangle has base on x-axis. Altitude from P is perpendicular to MN, which is vertical line through P: x = p. Altitude from M is perpendicular to PN. So we can find H as intersection of altitude from P (x=p) and altitude from M. Let's compute H.

Altitude from P: vertical line x = p.
Altitude from M: line through M perpendicular to PN. PN vector = N - P = (n-p, -p_y). So direction perpendicular to PN is (p_y, n-p) (since dot with (n-p, -p_y) is (p_y)(n-p)+(n-p)(-p_y)=0? Actually (p_y, n-p) dot (n-p, -p_y) = p_y(n-p) + (n-p)(-p_y)=0. So yes. So altitude from M: param (x,y) = (m,0) + t(p_y, n-p). Intersection with x=p gives: m + t p_y = p => t = (p-m)/p_y, provided p_y ≠ 0. Then y = 0 + t (n-p) = (p-m)(n-p)/p_y. So H = (p, (p-m)(n-p)/p_y).

Thus H = (p, (p-m)(n-p)/p_y). The line through H parallel to AP: AP is line through A and P. So we need to show that this horizontal line y = y_H = (p-m)(n-p)/p_y is tangent to circumcircle of triangle BEF.

Now, points: B=(x_A, -y_A). E and F: AP meets Ω again at E, and Γ again at F. Since A is on Ω, and line AP passes through A, the second intersection E is the reflection of A across the line through M perpendicular to AP? Actually for a circle with center M, the chord through A with direction AP has its midpoint on the line through M perpendicular to AP. So E is the point such that M is the midpoint of the segment joining the intersection points? No, the center is not necessarily on the line AP. However, we can compute E coordinates by solving |z-M| = r with z on line AP. Let's param line AP: A + s*(P-A). Since A is on Ω, we have s=0 gives A. The other intersection corresponds to s=s_E such that |A + s(P-A) - M| = r. Since |A-M| = r, we have |A-M + s(P-A)| = r. Squaring: r^2 + 2s (A-M)·(P-A) + s^2|P-A|^2 = r^2 => 2s (A-M)·(P-A) + s^2|P-A|^2 = 0 => s( 2(A-M)·(P-A) + s|P-A|^2 ) = 0 => s=0 or s = -2(A-M)·(P-A)/|P-A|^2. So E = A + s_E (P-A). Similarly, F = A + s_F (P-A) with s_F = -2(A-N)·(P-A)/|P-A|^2.

Thus we can compute E and F in terms of A,P,M,N.

Now, we need to prove that the horizontal line y = y_H is tangent to circle (BEF). So we need to compute the circumcircle of BEF. That is a circle through B, E, F. Since E and F are on line AP, and B is not on that line generally, the circle is determined. The center O_BEF lies on the perpendicular bisector of EF, which is perpendicular to AP. So O_BEF lies on a line perpendicular to AP through the midpoint of EF. That is a line. Also, O_BEF lies on perpendicular bisector of BE. So we can find O_BEF coordinates. Then the distance from O_BEF to the horizontal line y = y_H should equal radius.

This is still heavy, but perhaps the symmetry of the configuration with MN as x-axis and AP as some line may allow simplifications.

Another idea: Use coordinates but with a more clever parameterization that reduces the algebra. For example, set A=(0,0) and set the line AP as the x-axis. Then B=(u,v) with v≠0. So t_C = t_M - √(t_M^2+1/4). t_D = t_N + √(t_N^2+1/4). Then p is determined by the circumcenter conditions.

Now, we can try to compute p directly from the condition that P is circumcenter of ACD. Let’s write the equations:

PC^2 = PD^2 gives: 2v p + d^2(t_C+t_D)=0 (1). That is a linear equation in p.

Also, PC^2 = PA^2 gives: p^2 = (p - u/2 + v t_C)^2 + (v/2 + u t_C)^2. Expand: p^2 = p^2 - p u + (u^2/4) + 2p v t_C - u v t_C + v^2 t_C^2 + (v^2/4 + u v t_C + u^2 t_C^2). Cancel p^2: 0 = -p u + u^2/4 + 2p v t_C - u v t_C + v^2 t_C^2 + v^2/4 + u v t_C + u^2 t_C^2. Simplify: -p u + u^2/4 + 2p v t_C + v^2 t_C^2 + v^2/4 + u^2 t_C^2 = 0. Because -u v t_C + u v t_C cancel. So:

-p u + u^2/4 + 2p v t_C + (v^2+u^2) t_C^2 + v^2/4 = 0 => -p u + u^2/4 + 2p v t_C + d^2 t_C^2 + v^2/4 = 0. Thus:

p(u - 2v t_C) = u^2/4 + d^2 t_C^2 + v^2/4 = d^2/4 + d^2 t_C^2 = d^2(t_C^2+1/4). So p = d^2(t_C^2+1/4)/(u - 2v t_C). That is (2) from before.

Now, we can also express t_C in terms of t_M: t_C = t_M - s_M, where s_M = √(t_M^2+1/4). Then t_C^2+1/4 = (t_M - s_M)^2 + 1/4 = t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + s_M^2 + 1/4 = t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + (t_M^2+1/4) + 1/4 = 2t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + 1/2 = 2t_M(t_M - s_M) + 1/2 = 2t_M t_C + 1/2. Also, u - 2v t_C = u - 2v(t_M - s_M) = u - 2v t_M + 2v s_M. So p = d^2 (2t_M t_C + 1/2) / (u - 2v t_M + 2v s_M). That is messy.

[ (|M|^2-p^2)/2 - O_y m_y ] / (m_x-p) = [ (|N|^2-p^2)/2 - O_y n_y ] / (n_x-p). Cross multiply:

((|M|^2-p^2)/2 - O_y m_y)(n_x-p) = ((|N|^2-p^2)/2 - O_y n_y)(m_x-p).

This is linear in O_y. So we can solve for O_y. Then H = (p, y_H) with y_H = y_M + y_N - 2O_y? Actually y_H = y_P + y_M + y_N - 2y_O = 0 + m_y + n_y - 2O_y. So y_H = m_y + n_y - 2O_y. Then λ = y_H/v = (m_y + n_y - 2O_y)/v.

Let's attempt to verify the tangency condition using the expression for λ and the known relations. We'll work with the general coordinates A=(0,0), P=(p,0), B=(u,v). Now, we also have the relation from (2). Let's compute (2) in terms of t_M and t_N. We have t_C^2+1/4 = (t_M - s_M)^2 + 1/4 = t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + s_M^2 + 1/4 = t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + (t_M^2+1/4) + 1/4 = 2t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + 1/2 = 2t_M(t_M - s_M) + 1/2 = 2t_M t_C + 1/2. So (2) becomes: p = d^2(2t_M t_C + 1/2) / (u - 2v t_C). But also t_C = t_M - s_M. So u - 2v t_C = u - 2v(t_M - s_M) = u - 2v t_M + 2v s_M.

Thus we have:

p = d^2(2t_M(t_M - s_M) + 1/2) / (u - 2v t_M + 2v s_M) = d^2(2t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + 1/2) / (u - 2v t_M + 2v s_M). (Equation E1)

Now, we also have from (1): p = -d^2(t_M+t_N + s_N - s_M)/(2v). Equate these two expressions for p to get a relation between t_M,t_N,u,v. That relation might be what we need to verify that λ satisfies the quadratic.

Now, λ = [ m_y n_y - (p - m_x)(n_x - p) ] / [ u (n_x - p) + v n_y ].

We already computed numerator and denominator in terms of A = p - u/2. Let's recompute using the expressions for m_x,m_y,n_x,n_y.

Recall: m_x = u/2 - v t_M, m_y = v/2 + u t_M.
n_x = u/2 - v t_N, n_y = v/2 + u t_N.
A = p - u/2.

Then (p - m_x) = p - (u/2 - v t_M) = (p - u/2) + v t_M = A + v t_M.
(n_x - p) = (u/2 - v t_N) - p = (u/2 - p) - v t_N = -A - v t_N.
So (p - m_x)(n_x - p) = (A + v t_M)(-A - v t_N) = - (A + v t_M)(A + v t_N).

Now, numerator = m_y n_y - (p - m_x)(n_x - p) = m_y n_y + (A + v t_M)(A + v t_N).

Compute m_y n_y = (v/2 + u t_M)(v/2 + u t_N) = v^2/4 + (u v/2)(t_M+t_N) + u^2 t_M t_N.
(A + v t_M)(A + v t_N) = A^2 + A v (t_M+t_N) + v^2 t_M t_N.
So sum = A^2 + (u v/2 + A v)(t_M+t_N) + (u^2+v^2) t_M t_N + v^2/4 = A^2 + v( u/2 + A)(t_M+t_N) + d^2 t_M t_N + v^2/4.

Denominator = u (n_x - p) + v n_y = u(-A - v t_N) + v(v/2 + u t_N) = -u A - u v t_N + v^2/2 + u v t_N = -u A + v^2/2.
So denominator = v^2/2 - u A.

Thus λ = [ A^2 + v( A + u/2)(t_M+t_N) + d^2 t_M t_N + v^2/4 ] / [ v^2/2 - u A ].   (4)

Now, we also have p = A + u/2.

Now, we need to show that (λ - (2 t_M t_N+1/2))^2 = (t_M - t_N)^2 + (2 t_M t_N+1/2)^2.

This is equivalent to λ^2 - 2λ(2 t_M t_N+1/2) - (t_M - t_N)^2 = 0.

Alternatively, we can try to compute λ directly from the orthocenter condition using the circumcenter O of triangle PMN. Perhaps that yields a simpler expression.

Let’s attempt to compute O_y using the linear equations. From earlier:

O_x (m_x-p) + O_y m_y = (|M|^2 - p^2)/2.
O_x (n_x-p) + O_y n_y = (|N|^2 - p^2)/2.

We can solve for O_y by subtracting the two equations? Actually we can treat this as a system:

Let’s denote:

α1 = m_x-p, β1 = m_y, γ1 = (|M|^2 - p^2)/2.
α2 = n_x-p, β2 = n_y, γ2 = (|N|^2 - p^2)/2.

Then we have:

α1 O_x + β1 O_y = γ1.
α2 O_x + β2 O_y = γ2.

Solve for O_y. We can use determinant: Δ = α1 β2 - α2 β1. Then O_y = (γ1 α2 - γ2 α1) / Δ.

Now, we need to compute these quantities. We have:

m_x = u/2 - v t_M, n_x = u/2 - v t_N.
p = A + u/2.
So α1 = m_x - p = (u/2 - v t_M) - (A + u/2) = -v t_M - A.
α2 = n_x - p = (u/2 - v t_N) - (A + u/2) = -v t_N - A.

Also, m_y = v/2 + u t_M, n_y = v/2 + u t_N.
Now, |M|^2 = m_x^2 + m_y^2 = (u/2 - v t_M)^2 + (v/2 + u t_M)^2 = d^2(t_M^2+1/4). So |M|^2 = d^2 s_M^2, where s_M = √(t_M^2+1/4). Similarly, |N|^2 = d^2 s_N^2.

Thus γ1 = (|M|^2 - p^2)/2 = (d^2 s_M^2 - p^2)/2.
γ2 = (d^2 s_N^2 - p^2)/2.

Now, Δ = α1 β2 - α2 β1 = (-v t_M - A)(v/2 + u t_N) - (-v t_N - A)(v/2 + u t_M). Expand:

Δ = (-v t_M - A)(v/2 + u t_N) - (-v t_N - A)(v/2 + u t_M) = (-v t_M - A)(v/2 + u t_N) - (-v t_N - A)(v/2 + u t_M).

Compute each product:

(-v t_M - A)(v/2 + u t_N) = -v t_M * v/2 - v t_M * u t_N - A * v/2 - A * u t_N = -v^2 t_M/2 - u v t_M t_N - A v/2 - A u t_N.

(-v t_N - A)(v/2 + u t_M) = -v t_N * v/2 - v t_N * u t_M - A * v/2 - A * u t_M = -v^2 t_N/2 - u v t_M t_N - A v/2 - A u t_M.

Thus Δ = [ -v^2 t_M/2 - u v t_M t_N - A v/2 - A u t_N ] - [ -v^2 t_N/2 - u v t_M t_N - A v/2 - A u t_M ] = -v^2 t_M/2 - u v t_M t_N - A v/2 - A u t_N + v^2 t_N/2 + u v t_M t_N + A v/2 + A u t_M = (-v^2 t_M/2 + v^2 t_N/2) + (-A v/2 + A v/2) + (-A u t_N + A u t_M) + (-u v t_M t_N + u v t_M t_N) = (v^2/2)(t_N - t_M) + A u (t_M - t_N). So Δ = (v^2/2 - A u)(t_N - t_M) = -(v^2/2 - A u)(t_M - t_N). So Δ = (v^2/2 - A u)(t_N - t_M) = -(v^2/2 - A u)(t_M - t_N).

Thus denominator of O_y is Δ.

Now, compute γ1 α2 - γ2 α1 = γ1 * (-v t_N - A) - γ2 * (-v t_M - A) = -γ1(v t_N + A) + γ2(v t_M + A) = γ2(v t_M + A) - γ1(v t_N + A).

Plug γ1 = (d^2 s_M^2 - p^2)/2, γ2 = (d^2 s_N^2 - p^2)/2. So:

γ2(v t_M + A) - γ1(v t_N + A) = (1/2)[ (d^2 s_N^2 - p^2)(v t_M + A) - (d^2 s_M^2 - p^2)(v t_N + A) ].

Now, O_y = [γ2(v t_M + A) - γ1(v t_N + A)] / Δ = [ (1/2)( ... ) ] / [ (v^2/2 - A u)(t_N - t_M) ].

Then y_H = m_y + n_y - 2O_y. So y_H = (v/2+u t_M)+(v/2+u t_N) - 2O_y = v + u(t_M+t_N) - 2O_y.

Thus λ v = y_H = v + u(t_M+t_N) - 2O_y => λ = 1 + (u/v)(t_M+t_N) - (2O_y)/v.

Now, we also have that O_y = [ (1/2)( ... ) ] / Δ. So we need to compute O_y explicitly.

Let's compute the numerator:

N_y = (d^2 s_N^2 - p^2)(v t_M + A) - (d^2 s_M^2 - p^2)(v t_N + A).

We can also use the expressions for p and A. But maybe we can find a simplification using the relation between p and t_M,t_N.

Alternatively, note that the consistency condition from the two expressions for p gives a relation that might allow us to compute O_y in terms of t_M,t_N. Since O is the circumcenter of triangle PMN, and we have explicit coordinates, perhaps we can compute O_y directly using the fact that O lies on the perpendicular bisector of MN, which is line through midpoint of MN with direction (u,v). In our coordinate system, the perpendicular bisector of MN has equation: (x - (m_x+n_x)/2, y - (m_y+n_y)/2) is parallel to (u,v). So O = ( (m_x+n_x)/2 + μ u, (m_y+n_y)/2 + μ v ). Then we can find μ by requiring that |O-P|^2 = |O-M|^2. That gives an equation for μ. This might be simpler because we have expressions for m_x,m_y,n_x,n_y in terms of u,v,t_M,t_N.

Compute midpoint of M and N:

(m_x+n_x)/2 = ( (u/2 - v t_M)+(u/2 - v t_N) )/2 = u/2 - v(t_M+t_N)/2.
(m_y+n_y)/2 = ( (v/2+u t_M)+(v/2+u t_N) )/2 = v/2 + u(t_M+t_N)/2.

So param: O = ( u/2 - v(t_M+t_N)/2 + μ u, v/2 + u(t_M+t_N)/2 + μ v ). Let's denote:

X_O = u/2 - vS/2 + μ u, where S = t_M+t_N.
Y_O = v/2 + uS/2 + μ v.

Now, condition |O-P|^2 = |O-M|^2. P=(p,0). M=(m_x,m_y). So:

(O-P)^2 = (X_O-p)^2 + Y_O^2.
(O-M)^2 = (X_O - m_x)^2 + (Y_O - m_y)^2.

Set equal: (X_O-p)^2 + Y_O^2 = (X_O - m_x)^2 + (Y_O - m_y)^2.

Expand: X_O^2 - 2pX_O + p^2 + Y_O^2 = X_O^2 - 2m_x X_O + m_x^2 + Y_O^2 - 2m_y Y_O + m_y^2. Cancel X_O^2+Y_O^2: -2pX_O + p^2 = -2m_x X_O + m_x^2 - 2m_y Y_O + m_y^2. Rearr: 2(m_x - p)X_O + 2m_y Y_O = m_x^2+m_y^2 - p^2. But m_x^2+m_y^2 = |M|^2 = d^2 s_M^2. So:

2(m_x-p)X_O + 2m_y Y_O = d^2 s_M^2 - p^2. (Eq μ)

Now, we can plug in X_O and Y_O in terms of μ. Compute m_x-p = (u/2 - v t_M) - (A+u/2) = -v t_M - A. So m_x-p = -(v t_M + A). And m_y = v/2 + u t_M.

Thus Eq μ becomes:

2[-(v t_M + A)] X_O + 2 (v/2+u t_M) Y_O = d^2 s_M^2 - p^2.

But X_O = u/2 - vS/2 + μ u, Y_O = v/2 + uS/2 + μ v.

Plug in:

-2(v t_M + A)(u/2 - vS/2 + μ u) + 2(v/2+u t_M)(v/2 + uS/2 + μ v) = d^2 s_M^2 - p^2.

Simplify left. Expand each term:

First term: -2(v t_M + A)(u/2 - vS/2 + μ u) = - (v t_M + A)(u - vS + 2μ u) = - (v t_M + A)(u(1+2μ) - vS).

Second term: 2(v/2+u t_M)(v/2 + uS/2 + μ v) = (v+2u t_M)(v/2 + uS/2 + μ v) = (v+2u t_M) * ( (v+ uS)/2 + μ v ) = (v+2u t_M) * ( (v+ uS)/2 ) + (v+2u t_M) * μ v = (v+2u t_M)(v+ uS)/2 + μ v (v+2u t_M).

So left = - (v t_M + A)(u(1+2μ) - vS) + (v+2u t_M)(v+ uS)/2 + μ v (v+2u t_M).

Now, note that A = p - u/2. We also have p expressed in terms of t_M,t_N. Perhaps we can simplify by choosing μ such that the equation holds. This gives a linear equation in μ because the term with μ appears: from first term: - (v t_M + A)(2μ u) = -2μ u (v t_M + A). From second term: μ v (v+2u t_M). So coefficient of μ: -2u(v t_M + A) + v(v+2u t_M) = -2u v t_M - 2u A + v^2 + 2u v t_M = v^2 - 2u A. So the μ term is μ(v^2 - 2u A). Good. The constant term (no μ): from first: - (v t_M + A)(u - vS) = -(v t_M + A)(u - vS). From second: (v+2u t_M)(v+ uS)/2. So left = constant + μ(v^2 - 2u A). Thus:

constant + μ(v^2 - 2u A) = d^2 s_M^2 - p^2.

So μ = [ d^2 s_M^2 - p^2 - constant ] / (v^2 - 2u A). Where constant = -(v t_M + A)(u - vS) + (v+2u t_M)(v+ uS)/2.

Now, note that v^2 - 2u A = v^2 - 2u(p - u/2) = v^2 - 2u p + u^2 = d^2 - 2u p. So denominator is d^2 - 2u p.

Now, we also have the expression for p from (1): p = -d^2(t_C+t_D)/(2v). But perhaps we can compute μ directly using the known coordinates. This still seems messy.

Given the time, I think the best way to proceed is to present a coordinate proof that is complete, but we need to carry out the algebra. -d^2(t_M - s_M + t_N + s_N)/(2v) = d^2(2t_M t_C + 1/2)/(u - 2v t_C). Cancel d^2 (nonzero). Multiply both sides by 2v:

Given the heavy algebra, perhaps there is a more clever coordinate choice. Let's set the common chord AB as the y-axis. The points C and D are intersections of the x-axis (y=0) with Ω and Γ respectively, with order C,M,N,D. So C = (m - r, 0) = (m - sqrt(m^2+a^2), 0). Now, P is circumcenter of triangle ACD. A=(0,a), C=(c,0) with c=m-r, D=(d,0) with d=n+R. But P also lies on perpendicular bisector of AC. So we can find p_y.

Now, the line through H parallel to AP is horizontal: y = y_H.

Now, we need to show that this horizontal line is tangent to circumcircle of BEF. B=(0,-a). E and F are on AP.

Let’s compute E and F. AP line: param A + s*(P-A). A=(0,a), P=(p, p_y). So direction = (p, p_y - a). Then solve |A + s(P-A) - M| = r. Since |A-M| = r, we have:

r^2 + 2s (A-M)·(P-A) + s^2|P-A|^2 = r^2 => s(2(A-M)·(P-A) + s|P-A|^2)=0 => s=0 or s = -2(A-M)·(P-A)/|P-A|^2. So E = A + s_E (P-A). Similarly, F = A + s_F (P-A) with s_F = -2(A-N)·(P-A)/|P-A|^2.

Now, compute A-M = (0 - m, a - 0) = (-m, a). P-A = (p, p_y - a). So (A-M)·(P-A) = -m p + a(p_y - a). Similarly, A-N = (-n, a). So (A-N)·(P-A) = -n p + a(p_y - a).

Thus s_E = -2(-m p + a(p_y - a)) / |P-A|^2 = 2(m p - a(p_y - a))/|P-A|^2.
s_F = -2(-n p + a(p_y - a)) / |P-A|^2 = 2(n p - a(p_y - a))/|P-A|^2.

So E = (0 + s_E p, a + s_E (p_y - a)) = (s_E p, a + s_E (p_y - a)).
F = (s_F p, a + s_F (p_y - a)).

Now, we need circumcircle of BEF. B=(0,-a). So points: B(0,-a), E(x_E, y_E), F(x_F, y_F). Since E and F lie on line AP, and B is not on that line, the circle is determined. So the distance from O_BEF to the horizontal line y = y_H should be the radius.

So the numeric example works. Thus the algebra should hold generally.

Now, we need to present a rigorous proof. I think we can present a coordinate proof as follows:

- Place A at origin, line AP as x-axis. So P = (p,0) with p>0. Let B = (u,v) with v≠0. Without loss, assume v>0 (by reflection if needed). The line MN is the perpendicular bisector of AB, so its equation is ux+vy = (u^2+v^2)/2. Parameterize points on MN as (x,y) = (u/2 - v t, v/2 + u t). Let M = (u/2 - v t_M, v/2 + u t_M) and N = (u/2 - v t_N, v/2 + u t_N) for some real t_M, t_N. Since the radius of Ω is less than that of Γ and the order C,M,N,D on MN, we have t_M < t_N.

- Compute the distances: MA = r = d√(t_M^2+1/4), NA = R = d√(t_N^2+1/4) where d^2 = u^2+v^2. The points C and D are the intersections of line MN with Ω and Γ respectively, with the order C,M,N,D, so t_C = t_M - r/d = t_M - √(t_M^2+1/4), t_D = t_N + √(t_N^2+1/4). (We can note that t_C < t_M < t_N < t_D.)

- Since P is circumcenter of triangle ACD, we have PA = PC = PD. Using coordinates, these give two equations: from PC = PD we get 2v p + d^2(t_C+t_D)=0, and from PA = PC we get p(u - 2v t_C) = d^2(t_C^2+1/4). (These can be derived by squaring and simplifying.)

- From the first equation we obtain p = -d^2(t_C+t_D)/(2v). Substitute t_C and t_D to express p in terms of t_M, t_N, u, v.

- Now, compute H, the orthocenter of triangle PMN. The altitude from P is perpendicular to MN, and since MN direction is (-v,u), a perpendicular direction is (u,v). Thus H lies on line through P with direction (u,v): H = (p + λ u, λ v) for some real λ.

- The altitude from M is perpendicular to PN, so (H - M)·(N - P)=0. This yields a linear equation in λ. Solve for λ to obtain λ = [ m_y n_y - (p - m_x)(n_x - p) ] / [ u (n_x - p) + v n_y ], where M=(m_x,m_y), N=(n_x,n_y). After substitution and simplification, one obtains:

λ = [ A^2 + v( A + u/2)(t_M+t_N) + d^2 t_M t_N + v^2/4 ] / [ v^2/2 - u A ], where A = p - u/2.

- Now, we want to show that the line through H parallel to AP (i.e., horizontal line y = λ v) is tangent to circumcircle of triangle BEF.

- Points E and F: Since AP is x-axis, E is the second intersection of x-axis with Ω, so E = (2m_x,0). Similarly, F = (2n_x,0). (Because for circle with center (m_x,m_y) and passing through origin, intersection with x-axis gives (0,0) and (2m_x,0).)

- The circumcircle of BEF: B=(u,v), E=(2m_x,0), F=(2n_x,0). Its center can be found as the intersection of the perpendicular bisector of EF (vertical line x = m_x+n_x) and the perpendicular bisector of BE. A straightforward computation yields the center O = (m_x+n_x, (v^2/2 + (u^2+v^2) t_M t_N + u v (t_M+t_N)/2) / v?) Actually we can derive O in terms of t_M,t_N. Let's do that.

Given that m_x = u/2 - v t_M, n_x = u/2 - v t_N, and m_y = v/2 + u t_M, n_y = v/2 + u t_N. Also, we have that E = (2m_x,0) = (u - 2v t_M,0), F = (u - 2v t_N,0). So E and F are on x-axis. Then the circumcircle of BEF: Let O = (X, Y). Since EF is horizontal, the perpendicular bisector of EF is vertical line x = (x_E+x_F)/2 = u - v(t_M+t_N). So X = u - v(t_M+t_N). Also, O is equidistant from B and E. So:

(X - u)^2 + (Y - v)^2 = (X - x_E)^2 + Y^2.

Plug X = u - vS, with S = t_M+t_N. Then X-u = -vS. So left: v^2 S^2 + (Y-v)^2 = v^2 S^2 + Y^2 - 2vY + v^2. Right: (X - x_E)^2 + Y^2. x_E = u - 2v t_M. So X - x_E = (u - vS) - (u - 2v t_M) = -vS + 2v t_M = v(2t_M - S) = v(2t_M - (t_M+t_N)) = v(t_M - t_N). So (X - x_E)^2 = v^2 (t_M - t_N)^2. So right = v^2 (t_M - t_N)^2 + Y^2.

Set equal: v^2 S^2 + Y^2 - 2vY + v^2 = v^2 (t_M - t_N)^2 + Y^2 => v^2 S^2 - 2vY + v^2 = v^2 (t_M - t_N)^2 => Divide by v (v≠0): v S^2 - 2Y + v = v (t_M - t_N)^2 => 2Y = v S^2 + v - v (t_M - t_N)^2 = v ( S^2 - (t_M - t_N)^2 ) + v = v ( (t_M+t_N)^2 - (t_M - t_N)^2 ) + v = v (4 t_M t_N) + v = v (4 t_M t_N + 1). So Y = v (2 t_M t_N + 1/2). So O = ( u - v(t_M+t_N), v(2 t_M t_N + 1/2) ).

- The radius R_circ = distance from O to E: sqrt( (X - x_E)^2 + Y^2 ) = sqrt( v^2 (t_M - t_N)^2 + v^2 (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2 ) = |v| sqrt( (t_M - t_N)^2 + (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2 ). Since v>0, R_circ = v sqrt( (t_M - t_N)^2 + (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2 ).

- The line through H parallel to AP is horizontal: y = λ v. So distance from O to this line is |Y - λ v| = |v(2 t_M t_N + 1/2) - λ v| = |v| |2 t_M t_N + 1/2 - λ|. Since v>0, we need to show that |2 t_M t_N + 1/2 - λ| = sqrt( (t_M - t_N)^2 + (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2 ). Equivalently, (λ - (2 t_M t_N + 1/2))^2 = (t_M - t_N)^2 + (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2. This simplifies to λ^2 - 2λ(2 t_M t_N + 1/2) - (t_M - t_N)^2 = 0.

- Now, we need to verify that the λ obtained from the orthocenter condition satisfies this equation. To do so, we substitute the expression for λ in terms of A and the consistency condition from the circumcenter. We can show that λ = 2 t_M t_N + 1/2? But from numeric example, λ = y_H/v = -0.619/1 = -0.619, while 2 t_M t_N + 1/2 = 2*0*1 + 0.5 = 0.5. So λ ≠ that. So the quadratic is not simply λ = that constant; instead, λ satisfies that quadratic. So we need to show that λ is a root of that quadratic. That is an algebraic identity that can be proven by substituting the expressions for p and A and then using the relation between p and t_M,t_N from the circumcenter conditions.

Let's attempt to prove that λ satisfies (5) using the expressions we have. We have λ = [ A^2 + v( A + u/2)(t_M+t_N) + d^2 t_M t_N + v^2/4 ] / [ v^2/2 - u A ]. Let's denote:

We also have from (1) that p = -d^2(t_C+t_D)/(2v). But we might also have an expression for A from (2). Actually we can express A in terms of t_M,t_N,u,v by eliminating p. Let's try to derive a relation for A that simplifies the expression for λ.

From (1): p = -d^2(t_C+t_D)/(2v). So A = p - u/2 = -d^2(t_C+t_D)/(2v) - u/2.

Now, compute t_C+t_D = t_M - s_M + t_N + s_N = t_M+t_N + (s_N - s_M). So A = -d^2(t_M+t_N + s_N - s_M)/(2v) - u/2.

Now, also from (2): p = d^2(t_C^2+1/4)/(u - 2v t_C). And t_C^2+1/4 = 2t_M t_C + 1/2 = 2t_M(t_M - s_M) + 1/2 = 2t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + 1/2. So (2) gives p = d^2 (2t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + 1/2) / (u - 2v(t_M - s_M)) = d^2 (2t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + 1/2) / (u - 2v t_M + 2v s_M). So A = p - u/2 = d^2 (2t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + 1/2) / (u - 2v t_M + 2v s_M) - u/2.

Thus we have two expressions for A. Equate them to get a relation between t_M,t_N,u,v,s_M,s_N. That relation might be used to simplify λ.

Alternatively, we can avoid explicit use of p by computing λ directly from the orthocenter formula using the circumcenter O of triangle PMN. We have H = P + M + N - 2O. So λ v = y_H = m_y + n_y - 2O_y. Thus λ = (m_y + n_y - 2O_y)/v.

Now, O is the circumcenter of triangle PMN. Since P=(p,0) and M,N lie on line MN, we can find O using the perpendicular bisector of MN as before. Let’s use that. We have O = (X_O, Y_O) with X_O = u/2 - vS/2 + μ u, Y_O = v/2 + uS/2 + μ v for some μ (since O lies on perpendicular bisector of MN). The condition that |O-P|^2 = |O-M|^2 gives:

(O_x - p)^2 + Y_O^2 = (O_x - m_x)^2 + (Y_O - m_y)^2.

This is linear in μ. We can solve for μ and then compute Y_O. Then λ = (m_y+n_y-2Y_O)/v.

We already derived that μ = [ d^2 s_M^2 - p^2 - constant ] / (v^2 - 2u p). But we can also compute μ in terms of t_M,t_N, u, v, and p. This seems messy.

Given the time, I think we can present the coordinate proof by carrying out the algebraic verification in a structured way. Since the candidate solution already outlined the algebra, we can fill in the missing steps by showing that the identity (5) holds using the relations from (1) and (2). I'll attempt to do that.

Let's define:

Let’s denote:

We have t_C = t_M - s_M, t_D = t_N + s_N, with s_M = √(t_M^2+1/4), s_N = √(t_N^2+1/4). And p = -d^2(t_C+t_D)/(2v).

Now, compute A = p - u/2.

We have λ = [ A^2 + v( A + u/2)(t_M+t_N) + d^2 t_M t_N + v^2/4 ] / [ v^2/2 - u A ].

Now, we need to show that λ^2 - 2λ(2 t_M t_N+1/2) - (t_M - t_N)^2 = 0.

Let’s define:

Let’s compute the denominator: Denom = v^2/2 - u A. And numerator: Num = A^2 + v( A + u/2)(t_M+t_N) + d^2 t_M t_N + v^2/4.

We can also express A in terms of t_M,t_N, u, v. Let's use p from (1) to express A.

From (1): p = -d^2(t_M+t_N + s_N - s_M)/(2v). So A = p - u/2 = -d^2(t_M+t_N + s_N - s_M)/(2v) - u/2.

Thus A = -(d^2/(2v)) S - (d^2/(2v))(s_N - s_M) - u/2, where S = t_M+t_N.

Now, we also have from (2) that p = d^2(2t_M t_C+1/2)/(u - 2v t_C). But t_C = t_M - s_M. So 2t_M t_C+1/2 = 2t_M(t_M - s_M)+1/2 = 2t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + 1/2. And u - 2v t_C = u - 2v(t_M - s_M) = u - 2v t_M + 2v s_M.

Thus we have:

p = d^2 (2t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + 1/2) / (u - 2v t_M + 2v s_M). So A = p - u/2 = d^2 (2t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + 1/2) / (u - 2v t_M + 2v s_M) - u/2.

Equating the two expressions for A gives:

-d^2(t_M+t_N + s_N - s_M)/(2v) - u/2 = d^2 (2t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + 1/2) / (u - 2v t_M + 2v s_M) - u/2.

Cancel -u/2 on both sides. Multiply both sides by 2v:

-d^2(t_M+t_N + s_N - s_M) = 2v d^2 (2t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + 1/2) / (u - 2v t_M + 2v s_M).

Cancel d^2 (nonzero). So:

-(t_M+t_N + s_N - s_M) = 2v (2t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + 1/2) / (u - 2v t_M + 2v s_M).

Thus we have:

(t_M+t_N + s_N - s_M) = -2v (2t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + 1/2) / (u - 2v t_M + 2v s_M).   (Eq*)

Now, this is a relation between t_M, t_N, u, v, s_M, s_N. Note that s_M and s_N are defined by t_M,t_N. So this relation is an algebraic identity that must hold for the given configuration. We can use it to simplify λ.

Now, we need to compute λ. Let's compute λ in terms of t_M,t_N, u, v, and s_M,s_N. We have A = -d^2(t_M+t_N + s_N - s_M)/(2v) - u/2. So A = - (d^2/(2v)) (S + (s_N - s_M)) - u/2, where S = t_M+t_N.

Thus A = -(d^2/(2v)) (S + δ) - u/2, with δ = s_N - s_M.

Now, compute A^2. That will involve d^4/(4v^2) (S+δ)^2 + (d^2/(2v))(S+δ)u + u^2/4. But careful: A = - (d^2/(2v))(S+δ) - u/2, so A^2 = (d^4/(4v^2))(S+δ)^2 + (d^2/(2v))(S+δ)u + u^2/4.

Now, compute v(A+u/2)(t_M+t_N) = v( -(d^2/(2v))(S+δ) - u/2 + u/2 ) S = v( -(d^2/(2v))(S+δ) ) S = -(d^2/2)(S+δ)S.

So the term v(A+u/2)S = -(d^2/2)S(S+δ).

Now, the numerator Num = A^2 + v(A+u/2)S + d^2 t_M t_N + v^2/4.

Plug A^2: = (d^4/(4v^2))(S+δ)^2 + (d^2/(2v))(S+δ)u + u^2/4 + [ -(d^2/2)S(S+δ) ] + d^2 t_M t_N + v^2/4.

Thus Num = (d^4/(4v^2))(S+δ)^2 + (d^2/(2v))u(S+δ) - (d^2/2)S(S+δ) + u^2/4 + d^2 t_M t_N + v^2/4.

Combine the terms with (S+δ): (S+δ)[ d^4/(4v^2) + (d^2/(2v))u - (d^2/2)S ]. So Num = (S+δ)[ d^4/(4v^2) + (d^2/(2v))u - (d^2/2)S ] + u^2/4 + d^2 t_M t_N + v^2/4.

Now, denominator Denom = v^2/2 - uA = v^2/2 - u[ - (d^2/(2v))(S+δ) - u/2 ] = v^2/2 + (u d^2/(2v))(S+δ) + u^2/2 = (v^2+u^2)/2 + (u d^2/(2v))(S+δ) = d^2/2 + (u d^2/(2v))(S+δ) = (d^2/2)[ 1 + (u/v)(S+δ) ].

So Denom = (d^2/2)(1 + (u/v)(S+δ)).

Now, λ = Num / Denom. So λ = [ (S+δ)[ d^4/(4v^2) + (d^2/(2v))u - (d^2/2)S ] + u^2/4 + d^2 t_M t_N + v^2/4 ] / [ (d^2/2)(1 + (u/v)(S+δ)) ].

Multiply numerator and denominator by 2/d^2 to simplify:

λ = [ 2/d^2 * (S+δ)[ d^4/(4v^2) + (d^2/(2v))u - (d^2/2)S ] + 2/d^2 (u^2/4 + d^2 t_M t_N + v^2/4) ] / [ 1 + (u/v)(S+δ) ].

Simplify each term:

First term: 2/d^2 * (S+δ) * [ d^4/(4v^2) + (d^2/(2v))u - (d^2/2)S ] = (S+δ) * [ 2/d^2 * d^4/(4v^2) + 2/d^2 * (d^2/(2v))u - 2/d^2 * (d^2/2)S ] = (S+δ) * [ (2 d^2)/(4v^2) + (2/(2v))u - (2/2)S ] = (S+δ) * [ (d^2)/(2v^2) + (1/v)u - S ].

Second term: 2/d^2 (u^2/4 + d^2 t_M t_N + v^2/4) = (2u^2)/(4d^2) + 2 t_M t_N + (2v^2)/(4d^2) = (u^2)/(2d^2) + 2 t_M t_N + (v^2)/(2d^2) = (u^2+v^2)/(2d^2) + 2 t_M t_N = d^2/(2d^2) + 2 t_M t_N = 1/2 + 2 t_M t_N.

Thus λ = [ (S+δ)( d^2/(2v^2) + (S+δ)(u/v) - S(S+δ) + 1/2 + 2 t_M t_N ] / [ 1 + (u/v)(S+δ) ].

Now, note that (S+δ)(u/v) = (u/v)(S+δ). So the numerator becomes:

N = (S+δ)( d^2/(2v^2) ) + (u/v)(S+δ) - S(S+δ) + 1/2 + 2 t_M t_N.

And denominator D = 1 + (u/v)(S+δ).

Thus λ = [ (S+δ)( d^2/(2v^2) ) - S(S+δ) + 1/2 + 2 t_M t_N ] / [ 1 + (u/v)(S+δ) ] + (u/v)(S+δ) / [ 1 + (u/v)(S+δ) ]? Wait, careful: The term (u/v)(S+δ) is already included in the numerator; we have N = (S+δ)( d^2/(2v^2) ) + (u/v)(S+δ) - S(S+δ) + 1/2 + 2 t_M t_N. So λ = [ (S+δ)( d^2/(2v^2) + u/v - S ) + 1/2 + 2 t_M t_N ] / [ 1 + (u/v)(S+δ) ].

Now, recall that Eq* gives a relation between (S+δ) and the other variables. Eq*: S+δ = -2v (2t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + 1/2) / (u - 2v t_M + 2v s_M). But maybe we can also express u - 2v t_M + 2v s_M in terms of something. Note that s_M = √(t_M^2+1/4). So we might simplify 2t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + 1/2. That is 2t_M(t_M - s_M) + 1/2 = 2t_M t_C + 1/2. But we already used that.

Maybe we can also express d^2 = u^2+v^2. So d^2/(2v^2) = (u^2+v^2)/(2v^2) = u^2/(2v^2) + 1/2.

Thus the numerator term inside: d^2/(2v^2) + u/v - S = u^2/(2v^2) + 1/2 + u/v - S.

So λ = [ (S+δ)( u^2/(2v^2) + 1/2 + u/v - S ) + 1/2 + 2 t_M t_N ] / [ 1 + (u/v)(S+δ) ].

Now, we also have the relation from the consistency: (S+δ) = something. It might be possible to show that λ = something like (2 t_M t_N + 1/2) + something? But from numeric example, λ = -0.619, and 2 t_M t_N + 1/2 = 0.5, so λ is less than that. Actually the quadratic (5) is λ^2 - 2λ(0.5) - (t_M - t_N)^2 = 0. In the numeric example, t_M=0, t_N=1, so (t_M - t_N)^2 = 1. So quadratic: λ^2 - λ - 1 = 0. λ = (1 ± √5)/2 ≈ 1.618 or -0.618. And we got λ ≈ -0.619, which is a root. So λ = (1 - √5)/2. So λ is not simply 0.5.

Thus we need to verify that λ satisfies that quadratic. Perhaps we can compute λ directly from the expression for y_H using the orthocenter formula. But maybe there is a smarter way: Since the tangency condition is equivalent to the fact that the distance from the center of (BEF) to the line y = λ v equals radius, and we have expressions for O and λ, we can compute the squared distance and show it equals R^2. That is:

( Y - λ v )^2 = v^2 [ (t_M - t_N)^2 + (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2 ].

But Y = v(2 t_M t_N + 1/2). So left = v^2 (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2 - 2 λ v^2 (2 t_M t_N + 1/2) + λ^2 v^2 = v^2 [ (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2 - 2 λ (2 t_M t_N + 1/2) + λ^2 ].

Set equal to v^2 [ (t_M - t_N)^2 + (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2 ].

Cancel v^2. Then we need:

(2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2 - 2 λ (2 t_M t_N + 1/2) + λ^2 = (t_M - t_N)^2 + (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2.

Cancel (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2. So we need:

- 2 λ (2 t_M t_N + 1/2) + λ^2 = (t_M - t_N)^2.

Thus λ^2 - 2 λ (2 t_M t_N + 1/2) - (t_M - t_N)^2 = 0.

So we need to prove that λ is a root of that quadratic. That is the same as before.

Now, we have λ expressed in terms of S+δ and other variables. And we have Eq* relating S+δ to u,v,t_M,s_M. Also, note that we have not used the fact that the circle Γ has center N and passes through A, which gives the relation between t_N and s_N. But we already used that to define s_N. So the only relation we have is Eq*. That relation is a single equation linking t_M, t_N, u, v, s_M, s_N. Since s_M and s_N are defined, this equation is actually a specific algebraic relation between t_M and t_N. Perhaps we can derive from Eq* that (S+δ) is proportional to something like (t_M - t_N)? Let's try to compute using the numeric example: t_M=0, t_N=1, u=-1.618, v=1, s_M=0.5, s_N=1.118, S=1, δ=0.618, S+δ=1.618. Then Eq*: (t_M+t_N + s_N - s_M) = 1+1.118-0.5=1.618. Right side: -2v (2t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + 1/2) / (u - 2v t_M + 2v s_M) = -2*(0 -0 +0.5) / (u + 2s_M) = -1/(u+1) = -1/(-1.618+1)= -1/(-0.618)= 1.618. So indeed. Now, note that u+2s_M = u+1 = -0.618, and 2t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + 1/2 = 0.5. So Eq* becomes: S+δ = -2v *0.5 / (u+1) = -1/(u+1). So u+1 = -1/(S+δ). So S+δ = -1/(u+1). In our numeric, u+1 = -0.618, so -1/(-0.618)=1.618, yes.

Now, also we have that d^2 = u^2+v^2 = 3.618, and v=1. So d^2/(2v^2) = 1.809. Then u/v = -1.618. So d^2/(2v^2)+u/v = 1.809 -1.618 = 0.191. And S = t_M+t_N =1. So the term inside parentheses: d^2/(2v^2) + u/v - S = 0.191 - 1 = -0.809. Then λ = [ (S+δ)*(-0.809) + 1/2 + 2 t_M t_N ] / [1 + (u/v)(S+δ)]. (S+δ)=1.618, u/v=-1.618, so (u/v)(S+δ) = -1.618*1.618 = -2.618. Then denominator = 1 - 2.618 = -1.618. Numerator: 1.618*(-0.809) + 0.5 + 0 = -1.309 + 0.5 = -0.809. So λ = (-0.809)/(-1.618)=0.5. But we know λ = -0.619. So there is a mistake: Our expression for λ in terms of S+δ, etc., may be incorrect because we derived it from the earlier λ expression but we might have missed some terms.

Let's recalc λ from the earlier simplified expression:

We had λ = [ A^2 + v(A+u/2)S + d^2 t_M t_N + v^2/4 ] / [ v^2/2 - u A ].

We then expressed A in terms of S+δ. That gave:

A = -(d^2/(2v))(S+δ) - u/2.

Then A^2 = (d^4/(4v^2))(S+δ)^2 + (d^2/(2v))(S+δ)u + u^2/4.

v(A+u/2)S = v( -(d^2/(2v))(S+δ) - u/2 + u/2 )S = -(d^2/2)(S+δ)S.

So numerator = (d^4/(4v^2))(S+δ)^2 + (d^2/(2v))u(S+δ) - (d^2/2)S(S+δ) + u^2/4 + d^2 t_M t_N + v^2/4.

Denominator = v^2/2 - uA = v^2/2 - u( -(d^2/(2v))(S+δ) - u/2 ) = v^2/2 + (u d^2/(2v))(S+δ) + u^2/2 = (v^2+u^2)/2 + (u d^2/(2v))(S+δ) = d^2/2 + (u d^2/(2v))(S+δ) = (d^2/2)(1 + (u/v)(S+δ)).

So λ = [ (d^4/(4v^2))(S+δ)^2 + (d^2/(2v))u(S+δ) - (d^2/2)S(S+δ) + u^2/4 + d^2 t_M t_N + v^2/4 ] / [ (d^2/2)(1 + (u/v)(S+δ)) ].

Multiply numerator and denominator by 2/d^2:

λ = [ (2/d^2)*(d^4/(4v^2))(S+δ)^2 + (2/d^2)*(d^2/(2v))u(S+δ) - (2/d^2)*(d^2/2)S(S+δ) + (2/d^2)(u^2/4) + (2/d^2)d^2 t_M t_N + (2/d^2)(v^2/4) ] / [ 1 + (u/v)(S+δ) ].

Simplify each term:

Term1: (2/d^2)*(d^4/(4v^2)) = (2 d^2)/(4v^2) = d^2/(2v^2). So term1 = (S+δ)^2 * d^2/(2v^2).

Term2: (2/d^2)*(d^2/(2v))u = (2/(2v))u = u/v. So term2 = (u/v)(S+δ).

Term3: -(2/d^2)*(d^2/2)S(S+δ) = -S(S+δ).

Term4: (2/d^2)*(u^2/4) = u^2/(2d^2).

Term5: (2/d^2)*d^2 t_M t_N = 2 t_M t_N.

Term6: (2/d^2)*(v^2/4) = v^2/(2d^2).

So numerator of λ after scaling: N1 = (d^2/(2v^2))(S+δ)^2 + (u/v)(S+δ) - S(S+δ) + u^2/(2d^2) + 2 t_M t_N + v^2/(2d^2).

Now, u^2/(2d^2) + v^2/(2d^2) = (u^2+v^2)/(2d^2) = d^2/(2d^2) = 1/2.

Thus N1 = (d^2/(2v^2))(S+δ)^2 + (u/v)(S+δ) - S(S+δ) + 1/2 + 2 t_M t_N.

So λ = N1 / [ 1 + (u/v)(S+δ) ].

Now, in numeric example, d^2=3.618, v=1, so d^2/(2v^2)=1.809. (S+δ)=1.618, so (d^2/(2v^2))(S+δ)^2 = 1.809*(2.618)=4.736. (u/v)(S+δ)= -1.618*1.618 = -2.618. -S(S+δ)= -1*1.618 = -1.618. Then N1 = 4.736 -2.618 -1.618 +0.5 + 0 = 4.736 -4.236 +0.5 = 0.5 + 0.5? Actually 4.736 -4.236 = 0.5, plus 0.5 = 1.0. So N1=1.0. Denominator: 1 + (u/v)(S+δ)= 1 -2.618 = -1.618. So λ = 1/(-1.618)= -0.618. That matches λ = -0.618. Good.

So our expression is correct.

Now, we need to show that λ satisfies the quadratic. That is, λ^2 - 2λ(2 t_M t_N+1/2) - (t_M - t_N)^2 = 0.

We have λ = N1 / D1, where D1 = 1 + (u/v)(S+δ). So λ = N1/D1.

Then λ^2 - 2λ(2 t_M t_N+1/2) - (t_M - t_N)^2 = 0 becomes:

(N1^2/D1^2) - 2 (N1/D1)(2 t_M t_N+1/2) - (t_M - t_N)^2 = 0.

Multiply by D1^2:

N1^2 - 2 N1 D1 (2 t_M t_N+1/2) - (t_M - t_N)^2 D1^2 = 0.

Thus we need to verify that identity.

Now, we have expressions for N1 and D1 in terms of S+δ, u, v, d^2, t_M, t_N. Also, note that (S+δ) is related to u,v,t_M,s_M via Eq*. That relation can be used to eliminate (S+δ) and perhaps simplify.

Let's compute N1 and D1 in terms of S+δ. We have:

N1 = (d^2/(2v^2))(S+δ)^2 + (u/v)(S+δ) - S(S+δ) + 1/2 + 2 t_M t_N.
D1 = 1 + (u/v)(S+δ).

Now, note that S = t_M+t_N, and we also have the relation from the geometry: r = d s_M, and t_C = t_M - s_M. Also, from the circumcenter conditions we derived Eq*: (S+δ) = -2v (2t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + 1/2) / (u - 2v t_M + 2v s_M). That is a specific expression. But maybe we can also express S+δ in terms of u and v and t_M? Since δ = s_N - s_M, and s_N = √(t_N^2+1/4). That is not directly related to t_M. So Eq* is not a simple relation; it is the condition that p from (1) and (2) are equal. That condition is the consistency condition that must hold for the given configuration. So we can treat it as a relation that determines t_N given t_M,u,v. So it is not an independent variable; it is a specific function.

Thus to prove the identity, we can substitute the expression for S+δ from Eq* into N1 and D1, and then compute the resulting expression. That will involve t_M, t_N, u, v, s_M, s_N. Since s_M and s_N are defined, this becomes an algebraic identity in t_M, t_N, u, v, but note that t_N is not free; it is related by Eq*. So we can treat it as an identity that holds for the specific values that satisfy the geometry. To prove it generally, we need to show that the identity holds under the condition that the two expressions for p are equal. That is, we can start from Eq* and then derive the quadratic for λ.

Alternatively, we can avoid heavy algebra by using the fact that H is orthocenter and that the line through H parallel to AP is the line through H perpendicular to MN? Actually we already have that. Given the complexity, I think the best way to produce a rigorous proof is to present the coordinate proof with the algebraic verification, but we can present it in a more elegant way by noting that the tangency condition is equivalent to the fact that the power of H with respect to circle (BEF) is equal to the square of the distance from H to the center? Actually no.

Wait, we can also approach by using the fact that the line through H parallel to AP is the line through H perpendicular to MN (since AP is not necessarily perpendicular to MN; but we have altitude from P is parallel to AB, and that line is perpendicular to MN. So the line through H parallel to AP is not that altitude; it's horizontal in our coordinate system. In general, we want to show that the line through H parallel to AP is tangent to (BEF). This is a specific geometric statement that might be proved by angle chasing using cyclic quadrilaterals and properties of orthocenters.

Let's try to find a synthetic proof.

Given circles Ω and Γ intersect at A and B. Let M,N be centers. Line MN meets Ω at C, Γ at D. So C and D are points on the line of centers. Consider the circumcircle of ACD. Its center P is the circumcenter of triangle ACD. So P is the intersection of perpendicular bisectors of AC and AD. Since A, C, D lie on a circle with center P, we have PA = PC = PD.

Now, let E be the second intersection of AP with Ω. So A and E are on Ω, and AP is a line through A. Similarly, F is second intersection of AP with Γ. So A, E, F are collinear.

We need to prove that the line through H (orthocenter of triangle PMN) parallel to AP is tangent to circumcircle of triangle BEF.

Observations:

- Since M and N are on line MN, and P is on the perpendicular bisector of CD? Actually P is on perpendicular bisector of CD, which is perpendicular to MN. So line through P perpendicular to MN is the line through P parallel to the line through the midpoint of CD? That is not directly.

- The orthocenter H of triangle PMN: Since M,N are on line MN, the altitude from P is perpendicular to MN, so it is parallel to the line through the midpoint of CD? Actually the line through P perpendicular to MN is the line through P parallel to the perpendicular bisector of CD? No, the perpendicular bisector of CD is perpendicular to MN and passes through the midpoint of CD. So that line is exactly the line through P that is perpendicular to MN (since P lies on that perpendicular bisector). So the altitude from P in triangle PMN is exactly the line through P perpendicular to MN, which is the same as the perpendicular bisector of CD. So line through P perpendicular to MN is the altitude from P. Thus H lies on that altitude. So H lies on the line through P perpendicular to MN. That line is also the line through P that is parallel to AB? Because AB is perpendicular to MN, so line through P perpendicular to MN is parallel to AB. So H lies on line through P parallel to AB. Good.

- Also, the altitude from M in triangle PMN is perpendicular to PN. So H is intersection of altitude from P (line through P parallel to AB) and altitude from M.

Now, we want to show that the line through H parallel to AP is tangent to circle (BEF). So if we denote L as line through H parallel to AP, then L is parallel to AP. So the angle between L and something equals angle between AP and something.

Maybe we can show that the point of tangency is the reflection of H across something? Or that H lies on the polar of something with respect to circle (BEF).

Another idea: Use the fact that the circumcircle of BEF is the circle through the three points. Perhaps we can show that the line through H parallel to AP is the radical axis of two circles? Not sure.

Given the time, I think we can produce a coordinate proof that is rigorous and complete. Since the candidate solution already outlined the algebra, we can fill in the missing verification by showing that the identity holds using the relations from (1) and (2). I'll attempt to do that in a clean way.

Let's start from the expression for λ:

λ = [ (d^2/(2v^2))(S+δ)^2 + (u/v)(S+δ) - S(S+δ) + 1/2 + 2 t_M t_N ] / [ 1 + (u/v)(S+δ) ].

Let’s denote T = S+δ. Then:

λ = [ (d^2/(2v^2)) T^2 + (u/v) T - S T + 1/2 + 2 t_M t_N ] / [ 1 + (u/v) T ].

Now, we also have the consistency condition Eq*: T = -2v (2t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + 1/2) / (u - 2v t_M + 2v s_M). But maybe we can also express u - 2v t_M + 2v s_M in terms of T and other variables? Note that s_M = √(t_M^2+1/4). So we can write:

2t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + 1/2 = 2t_M(t_M - s_M) + 1/2 = 2t_M t_C + 1/2. And u - 2v t_M + 2v s_M = u - 2v t_M + 2v s_M. So Eq* gives:

T = -2v (2t_M t_C + 1/2) / (u - 2v t_M + 2v s_M). But t_C = t_M - s_M. So 2t_M t_C + 1/2 = 2t_M(t_M - s_M) + 1/2 = 2t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + 1/2. This is the same.

Now, we might also have a similar relation for t_N? Since we have t_D = t_N + s_N, and from the condition PC=PD we used that. But we haven't used that the circle Γ passes through A, which gives R^2 = n_x^2 + n_y^2, but that's already used to define s_N. So the only relation we have is Eq*. So we can treat T as a function of t_M, u, v, s_M. Then we can compute λ in terms of t_M, u, v, and also t_N, but note that t_N appears in S = t_M+t_N and in 2 t_M t_N. So we need to express t_N in terms of t_M, u, v, using Eq*. That is, we can solve Eq* for t_N.

From Eq*: T = t_M+t_N + s_N - s_M. So t_N + s_N = T - t_M + s_M. But s_N = √(t_N^2+1/4). This is an equation that determines t_N given t_M, u, v, and the relation from the denominator? Actually Eq* is a single equation linking t_M, t_N, u, v, s_M, s_N. Since s_M and s_N are defined, this is a specific equation. For a given t_M, u, v, we can solve for t_N. So we can treat t_N as a function of t_M, u, v. So the identity we need to verify is actually an identity in t_M, u, v (since t_N is determined). So we can attempt to prove that λ satisfies the quadratic by directly substituting the expression for t_N from the equation.

But Y = v(2 t_M t_N + 1/2). So left = v^2 (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2 - 2 λ v^2 (2 t_M t_N + 1/2) + λ^2 v^2. Set equal to v^2 [ (t_M - t_N)^2 + (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2 ].

Cancel v^2. Then we get:

(2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2 - 2 λ (2 t_M t_N + 1/2) + λ^2 = (t_M - t_N)^2 + (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2.

Cancel (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2. So we need:

- 2 λ (2 t_M t_N + 1/2) + λ^2 = (t_M - t_N)^2.

Thus λ^2 - 2 λ (2 t_M t_N + 1/2) - (t_M - t_N)^2 = 0.

Given the complexity, I'll try to present the coordinate proof with the algebraic verification, but I'll present it in a way that is clear and step-by-step, showing that the identity holds by substituting the expressions and using the relation from the circumcenter conditions. Since the candidate solution already outlined the algebra, I'll expand it.

I'll structure the proof as:

1. Set up coordinate system with A at origin, AP as x-axis, P = (p,0) with p>0.
2. Let B = (u,v) with v≠0. Without loss, assume v>0.
3. Parameterize line MN (perpendicular bisector of AB): points of the form (x,y) = (u/2 - v t, v/2 + u t). Let M = (u/2 - v t_M, v/2 + u t_M), N = (u/2 - v t_N, v/2 + u t_N). Since radius of Ω < radius of Γ, we have t_M < t_N.
4. Define d^2 = u^2+v^2. Then distances: MA = d √(t_M^2+1/4), NA = d √(t_N^2+1/4). The points C and D are on line MN at distances MA and NA from M,N respectively, with order C,M,N,D, so t_C = t_M - √(t_M^2+1/4), t_D = t_N + √(t_N^2+1/4).
5. Since P is circumcenter of ACD, we have PA = PC = PD. Compute these conditions:
   - PC^2 = PD^2 gives: 2v p + d^2(t_C+t_D) = 0 → p = -d^2(t_C+t_D)/(2v). (Equation 1)
   - PA^2 = PC^2 gives: p(u - 2v t_C) = d^2(t_C^2+1/4). (Equation 2)
6. From (1) and (2), we obtain a relation between t_M, t_N, u, v:
   Substitute t_C = t_M - s_M, t_D = t_N + s_N with s_M = √(t_M^2+1/4), s_N = √(t_N^2+1/4). After simplification, we get:
   (t_M+t_N + s_N - s_M) = -2v(2t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + 1/2) / (u - 2v t_M + 2v s_M).   (Equation 3)
   This equation is the consistency condition.
7. Compute the orthocenter H of triangle PMN. The altitude from P is perpendicular to MN. Since MN direction is (-v,u), a perpendicular direction is (u,v). Thus H lies on line through P with direction (u,v): H = (p + λ u, λ v) for some real λ.
   The altitude from M is perpendicular to PN. So (H-M)·(N-P)=0. Compute:
   (p+λ u - m_x, λ v - m_y)·(n_x-p, n_y)=0.
   Substitute m_x = u/2 - v t_M, m_y = v/2 + u t_M, n_x = u/2 - v t_N, n_y = v/2 + u t_N.
   After simplification, we obtain:
   λ = [ m_y n_y - (p - m_x)(n_x - p) ] / [ u (n_x - p) + v n_y ].
   Plugging in the expressions and simplifying yields:
   λ = [ A^2 + v(A + u/2)(t_M+t_N) + d^2 t_M t_N + v^2/4 ] / [ v^2/2 - u A ], where A = p - u/2.   (Equation 4)
8. Now, points E and F: Since AP is the x-axis, E is the second intersection of x-axis with Ω. For circle with center M and passing through origin, the intersection with x-axis gives (0,0) and (2m_x,0). Thus E = (2m_x,0) = (u - 2v t_M,0). Similarly, F = (2n_x,0) = (u - 2v t_N,0).
9. The circumcircle of BEF: Let O be its center. Since E and F lie on x-axis, the perpendicular bisector of EF is vertical line x = (x_E+x_F)/2 = u - v(t_M+t_N). So O = ( u - v(t_M+t_N), Y ) for some Y.
   Equating distances to B and E gives:
   ( (u - vS) - u )^2 + (Y - v)^2 = ( (u - vS) - (u - 2v t_M) )^2 + (Y - 0)^2.
   Simplify: v^2 S^2 + (Y-v)^2 = v^2 (t_M - t_N)^2 + Y^2.
   Expand: v^2 S^2 + Y^2 - 2vY + v^2 = v^2 (t_M - t_N)^2 + Y^2 → v^2 S^2 - 2vY + v^2 = v^2 (t_M - t_N)^2 → Divide by v (v>0): v S^2 - 2Y + v = v (t_M - t_N)^2 → 2Y = v S^2 + v - v (t_M - t_N)^2 = v( S^2 - (t_M - t_N)^2 ) + v = v(4 t_M t_N) + v = v(4 t_M t_N + 1). Thus Y = v(2 t_M t_N + 1/2). So O = ( u - vS, v(2 t_M t_N + 1/2) ).
   The radius R = distance from O to E: R^2 = ( (u - vS) - (u - 2v t_M) )^2 + ( v(2 t_M t_N + 1/2) )^2 = v^2 (t_M - t_N)^2 + v^2 (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2 = v^2[ (t_M - t_N)^2 + (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2 ].
10. The line through H parallel to AP is horizontal: y = λ v. The distance from O to this line is |Y - λ v| = |v(2 t_M t_N + 1/2) - λ v| = |v| |2 t_M t_N + 1/2 - λ|. Since v>0, we need to show that |2 t_M t_N + 1/2 - λ| = sqrt( (t_M - t_N)^2 + (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2 ).
    Equivalently, (λ - (2 t_M t_N + 1/2))^2 = (t_M - t_N)^2 + (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2.
    Cancel (2 t_M t_N + 1/2)^2 on both sides, we get:
    λ^2 - 2λ(2 t_M t_N + 1/2) = (t_M - t_N)^2.
    Thus we need to prove: λ^2 - 2λ(2 t_M t_N + 1/2) - (t_M - t_N)^2 = 0.
11. Now, substitute the expression for λ from (4). Let S = t_M+t_N, and let δ = s_N - s_M, so that T = S+δ = t_M+t_N+s_N-s_M. From (3), we have T expressed in terms of t_M, u, v, s_M. Also, from (1) we have p = -d^2 T/(2v). Then A = p - u/2 = -d^2 T/(2v) - u/2.
   Plug into (4): λ = [ A^2 + v(A+u/2)S + d^2 t_M t_N + v^2/4 ] / [ v^2/2 - u A ].
   Substitute A = -(d^2/(2v))T - u/2. Then A^2 = (d^4/(4v^2))T^2 + (d^2/(2v))u T + u^2/4.
   v(A+u/2)S = v( -(d^2/(2v))T - u/2 + u/2 )S = -(d^2/2)T S.
   Denominator: v^2/2 - uA = v^2/2 - u( -(d^2/(2v))T - u/2 ) = v^2/2 + (u d^2/(2v))T + u^2/2 = (v^2+u^2)/2 + (u d^2/(2v))T = d^2/2 + (u d^2/(2v))T = (d^2/2)(1 + (u/v)T).
   So λ = [ (d^4/(4v^2))T^2 + (d^2/(2v))u T - (d^2/2)T S + u^2/4 + d^2 t_M t_N + v^2/4 ] / [ (d^2/2)(1 + (u/v)T) ].
   Multiply numerator and denominator by 2/d^2:
   λ = [ (d^2/(2v^2))T^2 + (u/v)T - T S + u^2/(2d^2) + 2 t_M t_N + v^2/(2d^2) ] / [ 1 + (u/v)T ].
   But u^2/(2d^2) + v^2/(2d^2) = (u^2+v^2)/(2d^2) = 1/2.
   Thus λ = [ (d^2/(2v^2))T^2 + (u/v)T - S T + 1/2 + 2 t_M t_N ] / [ 1 + (u/v)T ].
12. Now, we need to show that λ satisfies the quadratic. That is, λ^2 - 2λ(2 t_M t_N+1/2) - (t_M - t_N)^2 = 0.
    Let’s denote L = λ. Compute L in terms of T and other variables. Write:
    L = [ (d^2/(2v^2))T^2 + (u/v)T - S T + 1/2 + 2 t_M t_N ] / [ 1 + (u/v)T ].
    Let’s also denote D = 1 + (u/v)T.
    Then L = [ (d^2/(2v^2))T^2 + (u/v)T - S T + 1/2 + 2 t_M t_N ] / D.
    Now, note that S = t_M+t_N, and we also have T = S+δ, with δ = s_N - s_M.
    The relation (3) gives T expressed in terms of u,v,t_M,s_M. We can also express u/v in terms of T and other variables? From (3): T = -2v (2t_M^2 - 2t_M s_M + 1/2) / (u - 2v t_M + 2v s_M). This can be rearranged to find u/v in terms of T and t_M,s_M. Alternatively, we can try to compute L - (2 t_M t_N+1/2) and then show that its square equals (t_M - t_N)^2 + (2 t_M t_N+1/2)^2.

    Given the algebraic nature, we can also note that the tangency condition is equivalent to the fact that the point H is the orthocenter and that the line through H parallel to AP is the line through H that is symmetric to the line through P parallel to AB with respect to something? Not sure.
